(V) Source of the Red Bandits

The reason why bandit suppression relies on the cooperation of the people of the whole country is that the commanders of the Red Bandits are directly the Chinese Communist Party and indirectly the Red Imperialists. They have a definite overall conspiracy, which is not to be equated with local bandits. The consistent conspiracy of the Third International towards China is to confuse the people of our country with communism, to cause peasants and workers to riot from time to time, and even to cause people in various professions to fight each other, in order to create a universal phenomenon of displacement and unemployment among the people of the whole country. Furthermore, from the universal phenomenon of displacement and unemployment among the Chinese people, they hope to cause economic panic and the collapse of industry and commerce in European and American countries. At that time, all the people in the world will be in a state of unemployment, and the Red Imperialists will be able to realize their ideal of world revolution. Therefore, no matter what the theory of communism that the Red Imperialists advocate, it is clear that they must first sacrifice the Chinese nation to provide resources for the European and American countries to vent their anger. Because the Red Imperialists have this kind of conspiracy, they support their so-called Communist Party members to implement various plans in China, such as colluding with warlords, fueling internal strife, inciting vagrants, anesthetizing young people, dividing the people, encouraging bandits, spreading rumors, and undermining local areas. Moreover, due to the past division of China by warlords, the exhaustion of the people's livelihood, the immaturity of knowledge, and the failure to complete the great cause of unification and peace at an early date, the various conspiracies and plans of the Red Imperialists were able to take advantage of the situation and secretly plant a part of their evil roots in society through the Chinese Communist Party members as tools, resulting in the disaster of the Red Bandits today. As evidenced by the information obtained by the government, the Chinese Communist Party, under the wings of the Red Imperialists, has set up a political bureau in the pseudo-central government, which is responsible for commanding the Red Bandits in various places and organizing Soviets in various places. Below it, there are the Yangtze River Bureau, the Southern Bureau, the Northern Bureau, the Manchurian Bureau, and the Jiangnan Provincial Committee (see attached table). Although what they currently consider most important is the Yangtze River Bureau and the Jiangnan Provincial Committee, hoping to seize the large cities of Shanghai and Wuhan as the center of their activities, it is difficult to guarantee that after repeated failures, they will not shift their attention to the south, north, and outside the customs, using their latent elements to make desperate moves, and the poison of the Red Bandits will spread throughout the country. From this, it can be seen that the Red Bandits today are actually a mixed body of Red Imperialists, outdated military personnel in our country, idle politicians, and local bullies, hooligans, and bandits. Their poison is enough to endanger the survival of the Chinese nation, harm the lives of the Chinese masses, and cut off the livelihoods of the Chinese people. It is not just the bandit areas that have been harmed that have suffered their poison.

Moreover, after the Red Imperialists invaded the Middle East Railway, the plan for China decided on July 15 last year not only used the weaknesses of the majority of poor and weak people in China and the long-term civil war to collude with vagrants and bandits in society as much as possible, to destroy rural order, to buy shameless literary beggars in literature and art, to promote so-called proletarian literature, and to promote communist banditry in politics, wanting to make China a country where people are unemployed, internal strife is endless, and trade between Asia and Europe and the United States is cut off, but also has active preparations in the military, in order to annex China and dominate it. The so-called active military plans are (1) to freely transport all kinds of personnel, weapons, and communist propaganda through the route from Soviet territory in Outer Mongolia, via Ulaanbaatar and Kalgan, to northern China; (2) to train the Mongolian army with Red Imperialist instructors and to replenish its latest combat equipment such as tanks and aircraft; (3) to secretly organize military forces among the Communist Party members of the Middle East Railway to prepare for the immediate disturbance of the northeastern provinces once a war breaks out; (4) to deploy two army corps of heavy troops in the Eastern Siberian Baikal Province, Heilongjiang, and Primorsky Krai to show intimidation and prepare for future operations. From this, it can be seen that the Red Imperialists' scheme to invade us is to use their strategy of internal response and external cooperation, and they must make the whole of China a colony of the Red Imperialists before they are finished. The Red Bandits in Hunan, Hubei, Jiangxi, and other provinces are actually acting as tigers for them to annex China in the guise of ancient-style bandits.

(VI) Conclusion

The complex causes of the Red Bandits are such, and the spread of the Red Bandit poison is such. Therefore, whether the Red Bandits can be eliminated is related to the life and death of the Chinese people and the survival of the nation from now on. It is by no means a minor matter involving only a part of the people or a political group. Since the government has made the determination to suppress the Red Bandits, it must consistently seek to implement it from beginning to end. However, how should the people of the whole country pool their wisdom and efforts to assist the government, eliminate all obstacles, and complete this task of stabilizing society and consolidating unification and peace? We must look forward to the National Assembly to give a clear and detailed direction.

Draft of Declaration on Abolishing Treaties Completed 14

To be Submitted to the Assembly for Discussion Today

(Nanjing) The Declaration on Abolishing Treaties will be submitted to the Assembly for discussion tomorrow. It is said that the wording is extremely cautious. The opinion of the drafting committee is that the National Assembly is not comparable to an ordinary free gathering. The words published should not only seek to be decisive and resolute. It should be fair and resolute in order to have strength. It should generally describe in detail the unequal treaties that violate international justice, the unreasonable shackles imposed on China, which endanger the survival and development of the nation, and that it is absolutely impossible to allow them to continue to exist. Based on the principle of changing circumstances, it should decisively

Domestic Urgent Telegrams

Declare their abolition and no longer recognize their validity. The government should strive to fully realize China's equality and freedom in the international community in accordance with the Prime Minister's teachings. (Special telegram on the 12th)

(Nanjing) The Declaration on Automatic Abolition of Treaties has been changed to the Declaration on Abolishing Treaties within a Time Limit in accordance with the adoption of the National Assembly. It will be discussed at the fifth general meeting tomorrow and then released. It is about a thousand words long. (Special telegram on the 12th)

(Nanjing) The Declaration on Abolishing Treaties, which is more than a thousand words long, has been discussed and deliberated by the drafting committee members Shao Lizi, Chen Bulei, Xiang Dingrong, Chen Cheng, Liu Luyin, and others in three late-night meetings. After the presidium members circulated and viewed it in turn, it was repeatedly added, deleted, and revised before the entire draft was completed. The presidium has decided to include it in the agenda of the fifth general meeting on the 13th as the first item for discussion. The wording of the full text is extremely cautious and the language is quite reserved. It can be passed and published without much modification. (Special telegram on the 12th)

(Nanjing) The content of the Declaration on Abolishing Treaties first states that unequal treaties violate international justice, then describes the pain of the Chinese state and people being bound by unequal treaties, and finally states the reasons why unequal treaties cannot but be abolished. It requests the government to announce the abolition within a time limit immediately. (Special telegram on the 12th)

Proposal for Continued Review 15

Two General Proposals Submitted to the Assembly

(Nanjing) The Proposal Review Committee held its third review meeting on the afternoon of the 12th. A total of 55 proposals were reviewed. The following were decided to be submitted to the assembly: (1) The three proposals by Deng Xun et al. on immigrating demobilized soldiers to engage in fundamental land reclamation, Liu Zuozhou et al. on ensuring national peace and unification, Fang Qingru et al. on reducing the army, determining the number of standing troops, and the standard for military expenditure, and Cheng Bin Yi et al. on incumbent military personnel not concurrently serving as local civil affairs officials, were consolidated into one proposal and submitted to the assembly. (2) The proposals by Ma Yinbing et al. on supporting the newspaper industry, Chen Jieshi et al. on lifting various restrictions on the newspaper industry, and Zhao Yushi et al. on the government earnestly promoting the newspaper industry, were consolidated and submitted to the assembly. It was also decided that eight proposals were not established. (1) The proposals by Ye Xiufeng et al. (A) that the government should expedite accurate statistics on the national economic situation and (B) that the government should promote research and inventions needed by society to connect facts, open research institutions, and facilitate patents. (2) The proposal by Wang Huanwu et al. on implementing the Factory Law within a time limit and supplementing the rules. (3) The proposals by Guo Mintie et al. (A) on deleting Article 20 of the Trade Union Law and (B) that trade unions of various industries should be organized in all provinces, cities, and counties. (4) The proposal by Liao Maoping et al. on determining the percentage of education expenditure and its sources. (5) The proposal by Li Zhishan et al. on forcing parents to strictly implement the education of their children. (6) The proposal by Zuo Duo et al. on implementing a conscription system. Three proposals were temporarily retained: (1) The proposal by Wei Shijun et al. on strictly prohibiting opium and severely punishing ineffective personnel. (2) The proposal by Pan Xiuren et al. on establishing large-scale woolen mills. (3) The proposal by Guo Yuchun et al. on requesting the allocation of the Boxer Indemnity for repairing the waterways in North China and the Huludao commercial port. Fourteen proposals were consolidated into suggestions to the presidium to be submitted to relevant groups for review: (1) The proposal by Zhang Dayi et al. on abolishing the Qinyu Railway loan contract and constructing the Guangdong-Yunnan Railway in advance. (2) The proposals by Pan Xiuren et al. (A) on constructing the Pingliang-Pangyuan and Baotou-Ningxia railways in advance, (B) on immigrating to and cultivating the Hetao area, (C) on excavating and repairing the old course of the Hetao Yellow River, and (D) on establishing large-scale timber yards. (3) The proposal by Zhang Zhijiang et al. on strictly implementing forestry and land reclamation and increasing production. (4) The proposal by Li Shengbo et al. on requesting the government to strictly implement protection and reward policies and ban foreign factories to save domestic goods. (5) The proposal by Yu Xiaochuan et al. on requesting the enactment of a stamp tax law. (6) The proposal by Yu Xiaochuan et al. on requesting exemption from coastal export taxes. Industrial Construction Program 16

Yesterday's Review Situation

(Nanjing) The Economic and Financial Review Committee held its second joint meeting at 3:00 PM this afternoon in the gymnasium of the Central University to review the government's proposal on the industrial construction program. Chairman Kong Xiangxi first discussed the original text of the proposal, and there was no objection from the audience. It was passed. Next, the committee reviewed the amendments of the representatives. The results were as follows: (1) Zhang Zhengxian proposed adding the Shashi-Xingyi line or the Guangzhou-Chongqing line and the Guangzhou-Dali-Tengyue line in the southwest railway system to the second item. (2) Hu Shuhua proposed (A) adding the Hankou-Chongqing section of the Sichuan-Han Railway to the Yuancheng Railway item and completing it by the end of the 25th year of the Republic of China, and (B) revising the original text of the sixth item to "The country must increase to more than 50,000 miles of aviation lines and 800 commercial aircraft by the 24th year of the Republic of China, and there must be two aircraft manufacturing plants, which the National Government will actively prepare and encourage." (B) Revise the original text of the eighth item to "Basic industries such as water conservancy, electricity, alkali, coal, sugar, kerosene, and gasoline should be actively handled by the National Government, and steel rails are essential materials for repairing railways, building ships, and manufacturing various agricultural and industrial machines. These two factories should be completed by the 25th year of the Republic of China. If private investment can be used to establish them, the government should encourage and assist them and provide them with definite guarantees." (3) Xu Zhen proposed adding the Harbin-Taonan line to the railway lines. (4) Ma Liang proposed adding the Zhangjiakou-Duolun line to the second item. (5) Wang Hanfang proposed adding cement and printing industries to the eighth item. (6) Liao Xiping proposed changing the order of the original plan as follows: (1) Principles, (2) Railways, (3) Highways, (4) Shipping, (5) Aviation, (6) Guiding the Huai River and governing the river, (7) Opening ports. Finally, it was resolved that the construction of railways should be handled by the National Government as soon as possible and completed within a time limit. The meeting adjourned at 6 o'clock. (Special Dispatch, 11th)

Proposal to Recover Outer Mongolia 19

(Nanjing) The proposal by Pan Xiuren et al. on recovering Outer Mongolia and Khulun as soon as possible to maintain the nation and strengthen the border: Outer Mongolia has a vast territory and abundant resources and has always been part of our country's territory. Since the Russian White Party Semyonov fled into Mongolia in the ninth year of the Republic of China, the Red Russians entered Khulun in the name of expelling Semyonov. Under the pretext of helping weak nations, they actually invaded Outer Mongolia. In fact, it is no longer ours. The Mongolians are ignorant and deceived by them, falsely claiming autonomy and sparing no effort to offer the great rivers and mountains to the Russians. All political power is held by the Russians. Although they are nominally independent, they are actually destroyed. The economic invasion they implement is even more vicious. There is a huge state-owned trade company, one is the Stermenka Company, which is completely operated by the Red Russians, and the other is the Xiehe Company, which is organized by Mongolian people with shares, but it is actually controlled by the Red Russians. Mongolia's business organization has always used a barter system, which has been handed down from generation to generation and is quite suitable. Since being Redized, the Soviet Union has prepared a ten-year plan for Mongolia, establishing leather factories, soap factories, chemical factories, and other factories, transporting the main products of Mongolia, fur, entirely to Russia, and not allowing them to be transported to China. They are especially able to oppress Chinese merchants trading in Mongolia. In the early years of the Republic of China, there were 200,000 to 300,000 Chinese merchants in Mongolia, but now there are only 2,000 to 3,000. What is even worse is that their cultural aggression policy against Outer Mongolia is even more pressing. They spare no effort in establishing schools and promoting Redization. Most of the Mongolian youth are forced to receive communist education and undergo strict military training. All Mongolian tribes have always believed in the Panchen Lama. Because the Red Russians found that the Panchen Lama was loyal to our country, they forced the Mongolians to shout the slogan "Down with the Panchen Lama." Cultural aggression is enough to destroy the country and the race. Korea and Taiwan are lessons from the past. Moreover, in recent years, the Red Russians have forced the Mongolians to sign secret railway agreements. The railway layout contract for seven lines has also been established, one from Ulan-Ude to Chita, one from Khulun to Uliastai, then from Uliastai to Biysk, and then from Uliastai to Kobdo, and then from Kobdo to Semipalatinsk, and to Urumqi, and from Urumqi to Olulu in Turkestan. The plan is meticulous, and their premeditation can be seen. The undercurrent of the Red disaster in the country is already a hidden worry, and Mongolia is actually existing in name only. It is a great sigh. According to our Republic of China, the five races are united, how can we let the Mongolians be trampled on like this for a long time? Now the Russian aggression policy is actually gaining an inch. In a few years, the northern border will no longer be ours. If Xinjiang, Yichang, and Suiyuan are lost, Shaanxi, Gansu, Shanxi, Hebei will be shaken, and national defense will become more dangerous. Looking forward, I can't help but worry. Therefore, preventing the Soviet Union from Redizing Outer Mongolia and Khulun is the top priority for saving the country and the nation today. Moreover, now the general public in Outer Mongolia, because they cannot bear the abuse and oppression of the Red Russians, are extremely eager for our country to recover it as soon as possible so that they can get rid of their suffering. This time, Special Envoy Mo Dehui went to Russia to negotiate only on the Chinese Eastern Railway and trade and diplomatic relations. I have not heard of any consideration of this important issue. The representatives are in the border area and feel deeply oppressed. They believe that if Outer Mongolia is not recovered quickly, the foundation of Soviet aggression will become increasingly consolidated, and it will be difficult to recover it in the future. This time's trade and diplomatic relations are equal to a futile effort. The tragedy of subjugation is imminent, and a moment's hesitation will be lost. The survival of the country is at stake, how can we sit idly by and make mistakes? Therefore, I hereby request the General Assembly to resolve to ask the National Government to find a way to recover Outer Mongolia as soon as possible to maintain the nation and strengthen the border. Is it appropriate? Please decide publicly. (Special Dispatch, 12th)

Proposal to Reduce Grain Tax 20

(Nanjing) Xiang Dingrong et al. proposed, I think that our country has valued agriculture since ancient times, but in recent years, the suffering of farmers has been twice as much as that of industry and commerce. Natural disasters such as floods and droughts are not to be mentioned. One is trapped by the high prices of everything, and daily use cannot be without needs. The other is trapped by the doubling of wages, and cultivation cannot be without assistance. The most painful thing is the sharp increase in land taxes and the unlimited surcharges. The urgent pursuit of taxes has been enough to discourage them and hasten their livelihood. The heavy land tax in the country is no more than Jiahu in Zhejiang and Susong in Jiangsu. At the beginning of the Ming Dynasty, autocratic monarchs heavily taxed our people out of spite and private resentment, charging several counties in the southeast with the grain tax that was unique in the country. In hundreds of years, although there have been successive reductions in taxes, the unfair tax has never been removed by revolution. At the beginning of the Republic of China, the temporary provincial assembly of Jiangsu and Zhejiang once discussed exempting the grain tax. Later, because the province's expenses were insufficient, it was changed to a discounted levy. At first, the discounted price of each stone of grain tax was three yuan, which still meant to exempt it from the levy. Recently, the price per stone has increased to seven or eight yuan, which has exceeded the selling price of new grains on the market, and the attached expenses for construction, education, etc., disaster relief, pest control, and land consolidation are increasing day by day. As a result, the total silver tax per mu of land is actually levied to one yuan and several corners, or even two yuan, which is heavier than the burden borne by farmers at the end of the Qing Dynasty. Coupled with years of famine and the decline of people's power, selling children and mortgaging wives to pay off this unfair burden is common. The purpose of the revolution is to help farmers and workers. Now, they do not benefit from it, but suffer from it first, which is very contrary to the wishes of the late Premier Sun Yat-sen. The National Government should order the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provincial governments to find out the amount of grain tax in each county with grain tax, the amount of discounted silver, and hurry to find a way to offset it. Before a way to offset it is found, the discounted price of three yuan per stone should be temporarily levied as in the first year of the Republic of China, and the additional taxes should not exceed 20% of the extra levy, in order to slightly relieve the people's power. When the offset is determined, the discounted grain tax in each county should be exempted immediately, so that the poison of autocratic monarchs will no longer exist under the revolutionary government. Some may suspect that if the grain tax is reduced and surcharges are limited, the provincial government's expenses will be insufficient. I don't know that taxation is based on the principle of fairness. If the tax is light, people will be happy to pay it. If the tax is heavy, they will accumulate arrears. In the northern provinces, the land tax is generally no more than ten copper coins. Every year, the collection is often fully paid. In the counties with grain tax in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, in the Qing Dynasty, only 80% was collected. Now, it is becoming heavier and heavier, and the arrears are becoming more and more. Why? The farmers' wealth is only this amount. Increasing the nominal amount will not help the actual situation. If the grain tax and surcharges are reduced separately, the number of arrears will be less and the number of payers will be more. The provincial government's expenses will definitely not be reduced because of this. Some also say that the government's recent policy of land tax collection will be based on land prices. This fair method can be used once and for all, and there is no need to discuss other methods. I don't know that land prices in the mainland are falling sharply. If the tax amount is determined and collected according to the current price, it will be really short. Moreover, the economic conditions and population of various places are different. Land in rich villages has high prices, and land in poor villages has low prices. It is difficult to find a standard, and the handling is tricky. It is better to gradually remove the most unfair of the current taxes. There is actual benefit to helping farmers, not empty words and decorations, which is easier to start. This is the general idea of reducing grain tax and limiting surcharges to help farmers. Is it feasible? It should be decided publicly.

Haihe Short-Term Public Bonds 30

The Fund Custody Committee Will Be Reorganized

(Nanjing) The Hebei Haihe Project Short-Term Public Bonds Fund Custody Committee will be reorganized separately. The rest will be elected, and three standing committee members will be elected from among the seven to manage the day-to-day affairs. It will be established on June 1. As for the underwriting of the public bonds, the China, Communications, Salt, Continental, Jin Cheng, China South, and Hebei Provincial banks of Tianjin and Beijing will be responsible for soliciting subscriptions, accounting for three-quarters of the total amount. On the foreign bank side, the French Industrial and Commercial Bank of Tianjin and Beijing will be responsible for soliciting subscriptions for one-quarter of the total amount. (Nanjing) The contract for the Sino-Japanese Chuandanshui Line expired at the end of last month. The contents are: (1) Temporary loan line, (2) distribution of telegram prices, (3) rights of receipt and dispatch, (4) standard for over-the-line prices. As for the right of landing on the line, the Japanese Commissioner requested to reserve it for future discussion. Hu Ruoyu Takes Office as Superintendent of Kailuan Coal Mine 34

All Five Mines Go on Strike

The Provincial Government Tries to Mediate

(Beiping) Hu Ruoyu took office as Superintendent of the Kailuan Coal Mine in Tianjin today. After taking office, he will seek a solution to the recent disputes in Kailuan. (Special Dispatch, 12th)

(Beiping) After all Kailuan miners went on strike on the 11th, the Hebei Provincial Rectification Committee sent Su Baicheng to investigate. Su set off on the 13th. This strike was completely instigated by the Mine Bureau. Because the Mine Road issue has not been resolved, the Mine Bureau wants to use the strike to resolve the Mine Road dispute. The reason is very complicated and it may be difficult to resolve it for a while. The workers plan to mine coal themselves to maintain their livelihood. (Special Dispatch, 12th)

(Nanjing) The issue of the dispute between Kailuan Mine and the Beining Road, the Road Bureau claims that the Mine should pay 1.38 million yuan for the delayed settlement fee and 800,000 yuan for the coal weight handling fee. The Mine only agrees to pay 500,000 yuan for the settlement. The Road Bureau believes that it is suffering too much and must calculate according to the case. Recently, Kailuan is imposing itself. It has sent people to mediate, hoping to increase the delayed fee by a few yuan, but does not agree to pay 0.3 yuan per ton for the handling fee. The Road Bureau still insists on its original proposal because there is a precedent on the Jinpu Road. The case has not made any progress, and the Kailuan strike is also fundamentally unresolved because of this. (Special Dispatch, 12th)

(Tianjin) The Kailuan Mine General Trade Union issued a declaration on the 11th because the Bureau did not respond to the request to cancel the two-day weekly shutdown. All five mines went on strike. The Provincial Government sent Ding Zhanhai and Guo Shaoyi to Tangshan to convene a meeting of representatives from both labor and management on the 14th to mediate together with the local Public Security Bureau. However, the attitude of the capital side is tough, and it may not be easy to resolve it for a while. There are no less than 50,000 workers in the entire mine, who are forced to make a living and are easily incited by the Communist Party. This matter is worthy of attention. (Special Dispatch, 12th)

Important Foreign Telegrams

Riots in Spain, Monasteries and Churches Suffer 60

Martial Law Declared in the Capital, Order Gradually Restored

A Setback at the Beginning of the Establishment of the Republic

Foreign Minister Lerroux Departs for Geneva

Berenquer Arrested Again After Just Being Released

Reuters, Madrid, 12th: This morning the situation here is normal, but soldiers are still stationed at various key points. The police have arrested 26 people and recovered the weapons stolen yesterday. Prime Minister Zamora issued a statement, admitting to a setback, but said that the government would not allow a repeat of yesterday's events. Freedom of belief would be respected, but all religious sites would be protected. He also urged the public to work as usual. The directors of the Socialist Party and the General Confederation of Labor have issued notices denouncing the excesses and urging workers to resume work immediately.

Reuters, Madrid, 12th: Entertainment venues and cafes are now operating as usual. Foreign Minister Lerroux set off for Geneva yesterday morning to attend the League of Nations administrative meeting. He turned back halfway upon hearing the news of the riots and has now set off again. It is reported that the provinces are still quiet.

Reuters, Madrid, 11th: Official sources say that a total of ten monasteries and churches have been destroyed. The Minister of the Interior stated today that the government is determined to eradicate this lawless behavior. Troops stationed outside Madrid have been transferred back to the city. The Catholic newspaper "Debate" has been ordered to cease publication by the government. The government has ordered officials throughout the country to actively prevent the spread of unrest. It is reported that former Prime Minister Berenguer has been arrested again after the declaration of martial law and is being held in a military prison. Tonight, the situation in Madrid suddenly changed, and the calls for destruction abruptly ceased. Shops have reopened, and the city has returned to normal, except for soldiers patrolling the streets. Catholics had prepared for today's disturbances and are said to have sent their documents and valuables to Rome and other places months ago. When the unrest first broke out, women emerged from monasteries disguised as country women, who were actually nuns. They had prepared simple and suitable secular women's clothing in advance, so they were able to change clothes and escape before the monasteries were burned. Although at least five monasteries have been burned down, no one was hurt. The cabinet has been meeting all day, and the Minister of the Interior stated in the evening that these riots were merely a suicidal act by the restoration party and the Communist Party, and the government is determined to stop them. Reuters, Cordoba, 11th: This morning, crowds here threw stones at several churches and monasteries, and a Catholic newspaper office was also attacked. Demonstrators shouted "Death to Archbishop Segura and Dr. Apina!" A Catholic school was also pelted with bricks, but although the school gate was open, the crowd did not enter. Order was later restored. Local streetcar drivers have gone on strike, following the example of the Madrid streetcar drivers.

Briand Most Likely to Win French Presidential Election 61

National News Agency, Paris, 11th: The French presidential election is scheduled to be held on Wednesday. The new president will be inaugurated on June 13th for a term of seven years. As usual, there is no vice president. National News Agency, Paris, 11th: This evening, Foreign Minister Briand met with representatives of left-wing groups from the Senate and the Chamber of Deputies and announced that he had accepted the nomination for the election. He said that if he were to be elected president, he would go to Geneva on May 15th for a few days, but would not participate in the Pan-European Conference or be involved in preparing for the conference. His sole purpose is to bid farewell to the diplomatic representatives of various countries. Briand is the most experienced and qualified person on the French political stage. His entry into the presidential election is by no means a rash attempt. He must have a well-thought-out plan and a predetermined victory. Therefore, only Briand and Senate President Doumer are the most likely candidates for the presidential election.

Reuters, Paris, 11th: Briand has agreed to be a presidential candidate. Senate President Doumer is also a presidential candidate. He expressed his opinion today, saying that Briand is more useful to the country as Foreign Minister than as President. For this reason, he is unwilling to concede, but hopes that the electors will choose for themselves. Senator Hennessy has also agreed to be a presidential candidate.

British Government's Attitude Towards China's Automatic Treaty Abolition 62

Reuters, London, 11th: British Foreign Secretary Henderson said in the House of Commons today in response to a member's question that, according to a report from the British Minister to China, Sir Lampson, the Chinese government issued an order on May 4th to abolish the consular jurisdiction enjoyed by foreigners, effective January 1st of next year. However, this order has not been officially delivered to the British Minister, so he has not received the original text. Negotiations are still ongoing. Documents regarding this matter are not yet convenient to be published in the House of Commons. Former Foreign Secretary Chamberlain said that since China has issued this order, the situation has changed, so the diplomatic authorities can report the negotiation process to the House of Commons. Henderson replied that he did not think it appropriate. He had previously stated that if the treaty is agreed upon, the House of Commons may have a detailed debate during the ratification. Conservative Party member Wood said that this important order is very important to many people in other countries. Why was it published in the newspaper instead of being delivered to the diplomatic authorities of various countries? He asked the Foreign Secretary to investigate. Henderson replied that he was not in a position to interfere with the way other governments publish news.

Sir John Simon Criticizes Hong Kong's Mui-Tsai System 66

Undersecretary of State for the Colonies Defends Hong Kong Government

Reuters, London, 11th: Sir John Simon, a key figure in the Liberal Party, strongly criticized Hong Kong's Mui-Tsai system in the House of Commons today, while Undersecretary of State for the Colonies, Shiels, vigorously defended the Hong Kong government. At the beginning of his speech, Sir John Simon took out a Chinese-style sales contract for the sale of a nine-year-old girl for 110 Hong Kong dollars. Sir John Simon said that this is no longer a national issue, because there is an international movement against slavery, and Britain is its leader. Shiels replied that, as a general rule, the treatment of Mui-Tsai is currently not bad. Chinese public opinion expects those who keep Mui-Tsai to let the Mui-Tsai marry when they are eighteen years old, or to provide them with appropriate preparation. If any money is paid, it is strictly prohibited by the Hong Kong Domestic Servants Ordinance of 1923. The Hong Kong Mui-Tsai system is different from slavery. The number of Mui-Tsai has decreased by 50% in the past eight years, so the number of registrations has decreased significantly compared to before. It will definitely continue to decrease and eventually be eliminated. This is the intention of the Governor of Hong Kong in consultation with the Colonial Secretary. There is a police inspector who specializes in investigating Mui-Tsai. The Governor of Hong Kong and Chinese charitable organizations have taken measures to protect the happiness of Mui-Tsai, and the Hong Kong government has adopted various reasonable steps to implement the government's policy on this matter. Before taking office, the Colonial Secretary had informed the new Governor of Hong Kong, Sir Peel, of the importance of thoroughly implementing the Mui-Tsai Management Ordinance. Members of various parties in the House of Commons expressed disapproval of the Hong Kong Mui-Tsai system. Therefore, when concluding this debate, Shiels earnestly stated that the Colonial Department will eliminate this system in every possible way.

He appealed the matter, and the High Court has now deemed the lower court's judgment to be too lenient and has changed the sentence to two months in prison.

Chimney Percher in Extremely Critical Condition 68

Reuters, Tokyo, 12th: Chiba has been exposed to the sun and rain since climbing the chimney on May 1st and is in extremely critical condition. This morning, a union lawyer, accompanied by two of Chiba's comrades, braved heavy rain to climb to the top of the chimney and urged Chiba to come down. They saw that Chiba was almost too weak to stand. They brought a basket and 500 feet of rope to lower Chiba, but Chiba, although having suffered for many days, remained unmoved and would not come down until the strikers had achieved their goal. In the afternoon, two of his comrades again climbed the chimney with a change of clothes and a small tent to help him change out of his wet clothes and to set up the tent to protect him from the wind and rain. At 4:30 p.m., a doctor climbed to the top of the chimney and injected him with camphor. The doctor descended after examining Chiba and said that Chiba's condition is currently stable, but if he continues to stay in a high place and sleep in the open air, his life expectancy may not be prolonged. Chiba is only nineteen years old, and his strong will is admirable. As for the workers who have been on a hunger strike, there has been no respite since April 21st. About 50 people have been sent to the hospital due to weakness from prolonged hunger.

Jiangxi Finance Loses Over 8 Million in the 19th Year 72

Ministry of Finance Decides to Implement Business Tax

Nanchang Dispatch: The budgeted revenue and expenditure of Jiangxi Province are both 14 million yuan, but since the communists are all over the country, the revenue is generated in only over ten counties such as Linchuan, Jinxian, Jiujiang, and Nanchang, totaling less than 30-40% of the budget. And after the implementation of eliminating likin and turning over the salt surcharge to the central government, revenue is further reduced by hundreds of thousands of yuan per month. At the same time, due to the suppression of communists, grain transport, and post-war reconstruction in communist areas,

News Summary 73

And Editor: Security forces, self-defense corps, etc., urgently need funds, and expenditures have surged. As of now in the 19th year of the Republic [1930], the deficit is approximately 7 million yuan. Arrears to various government agencies for administrative expenses have accumulated for several months, with some payments dating back to October of last year still outstanding. Beggar asylums and homes for the disabled and elderly receive only a few hundred yuan per month in funding, and these too are in arrears for several months. Consequently, large groups of disabled beggars are staging protests everywhere, waving banners and seeking relief. Furthermore, many individuals holding payment orders from the treasury are seeking redemption. Several days ago, the Provincial Government's general affairs staff even had a major conflict with the treasurer over the lack of funds to purchase tea leaves, highlighting the dire financial straits. Fortunately, the educational expense circulation notes and financial treasury note funds have been allocated by the Ministry of Finance from the salt surtax revenue. Therefore, the education sector seems to have found new hope after facing a dead end. The two types of notes had previously experienced a temporary surge in value, with circulation notes rising from 75% of face value to 98%. However, in recent days, due to the diversion of funds intended for redemption by the Provincial Department of Finance, they have resumed their decline. Short-term treasury notes, originally intended as a fund for the autumn grain transport, have also fallen to 55% because no grain can be collected from the bandit areas and the provincial treasury is required to allocate administrative expenses instead. The Provincial Department of Finance hopes to use central government subsidies and the opening of business tax as life-saving measures. Regarding central government subsidies, various sectors in the province have repeatedly appealed. The Director of the Department of Finance, Huang Bozhong, has gone to Beijing several times to petition. The Minister of Finance, Song, finally agreed to provide 40,000 yuan per month, in addition to the two educational fund notes, stating that this would only last until October. This is merely a drop in the bucket and does not solve the problem. As for the more than 3 million yuan in military expenses that the province previously advanced for the central government, there is still no news of repayment despite repeated demands. The regulations and rules for the collection of business tax have long been passed. It is estimated that more than 100,000 yuan will be collected in Nanchang, Jiujiang and other places with the establishment of bureaus; more than ten places such as Hekou will set up tax offices with less than 100,000 yuan; thirty-six counties will be handled by the local financial bureaus. However, the business community in the province has submitted petitions one after another requesting a postponement of the business tax due to the devastation of the bandit scourge and the decline of all industries. Nevertheless, the Department of Finance, in order to make up for government expenses, has decided to implement it and has decided to start from Nanchang and Jiujiang first, while bandit areas will be temporarily postponed.

Li Mingzhong Telegraphs Details of Bandit Suppression 74

Remnants of Bandit Forces in Hubei Flee to Anhui Border

Hankou Correspondence: Li Mingzhong, the Pacification Commissioner of the border region of the three provinces of Henan, Anhui, and Hubei, after receiving the order to encircle and suppress bandit forces, immediately moved the Commissioner's Office to Hanchuan to facilitate command. He also ordered the divisions of Ji Hongchang, Zhang Yinxiang, Ge Yunlong, Fan Xiji, Xia Douyin, and Xiao Zhichu to jointly launch a general offensive with the two divisions of Zhao Guantao stationed in Xinyang and Dai Minquan stationed in Gushi. After several fierce battles, the main force of the bandits was finally defeated. The important passes occupied by the bandit forces, such as Bopi River, Xinji, Qiliping, and Xuanhua Store, were also successively recovered. All the pseudo-organizations such as the Soviet government of the special zone of the three provinces of Henan, Anhui and Hubei and the Rural Soviet government were destroyed. Important members of the pseudo-government, military inspectors of the pseudo-special zone, and instructors of military transport in the special zone were all shot on the spot. On the 6th, a major organ of the Red bandits was uncovered in Hanchuan City, and a recent secret riot plan and a copy of the pseudo-central government's defense strategy for the second meeting of the National Army were seized. They were immediately sent to the Wuhan headquarters and forwarded to the General Headquarters for record. As for the remnants of the bandit forces, it was reported that they had fled to the border of Anhui. Li Mingzhong therefore ordered Ji Hongchang to lead his division to track down and pursue the bandits to eliminate them completely. At the same time, he reported the course of successive battles to General Commander Jiang and Director He of the Wuhan headquarters. The original telegram is as follows: "Director He of the Wuhan Headquarters, esteemed: According to the telegram from Chief Commander Ji Hongchang, the situation of pursuing and suppressing the Red bandits is as follows: (1) The Red bandits entrenched in the border area of Henan, Hubei and Anhui occupy Bopi River, Xinji, Qiliping, Xuanhua Store, etc. It is the entire 1st, 14th, and 15th armies, the entire Independent 3rd Division, and a part of the Guard Brigade, totaling about 45,000 people. The local farmers have all become Red slaves. (2) I have been ordered to lead the 30th, 31st, and 23rd divisions to fight fiercely with the Red bandits and Red slaves in Bopi River, Huwan, Xinji, Shuangshan, Changjian Factory River, Yuanshugang, Qiliping, Gufengling, Huangpi Dian, Xuanhua Store and other places for ten days from April 22. All the above places have been successively occupied, and about 600 square miles of land have been recovered. Most of the remnant bandits have fled to the Anhui border. (3) In all battles, about 6,000 to 7,000 enemies were killed, one pseudo-commander and one pseudo-captain were killed, and 797 bandits were captured, including many female bandits in yellow military uniforms, who have all been executed. (4) Successively captured 4 mortars, 1 mountain gun, 1 radio, more than 200 miscellaneous guns, 136 shells, more than 13,000 miscellaneous gun bullets, and countless knives and spears. (5) Our army lost 1 battalion commander and 1 battalion staff officer, 4 company and platoon leaders, 172 soldiers, and more than 40 militiamen; 3 battalion commanders, 5 battalion staff officers, 21 company and platoon leaders, 419 soldiers, and 59 militiamen were injured. In addition to ordering the Chief Commander to make some replenishment and then pursue the bandits to the Anhui border, I respectfully report. Li Mingzhong kowtows. (May 11)"

The "May Ninth National Humiliation Day" Meeting of All Circles in Jinan 75

Japanese Impersonate Our Workers to Enter Venue

The Masses Resolved to Submit Two Proposals to the National Assembly

Jinan Correspondence: May 9th is the National Humiliation Memorial Day for Yuan Shikai's acceptance of Japan's Twenty-One Demands. Unexpectedly, when all circles in Jinan held a meeting to commemorate it, the Japanese consul in Jinan actually dispatched detectives to impersonate our workers and sneak into the meeting to gather information and plot disturbances, which can be said to be extremely rogue. On this day (9th), all circles in Jinan, in commemoration of May 9th, not only lowered the flag to half-mast throughout the city to express condolences and stop entertainment banquets, but also held a citizens' assembly at the Jinan Municipal Government at 9 am. As early as 7 o'clock in the morning, people from all walks of life, officials from various agencies, and students from various schools lined up to attend the meeting, holding small flags with various slogans written on them, totaling more than 300 groups and about 50,000 people, with an extremely tragic atmosphere. The presidium of the conference was composed of Wang Yumin of the Provincial Reorganization Committee, Chen Weixin of the Provincial Government, He Shenzhai of the Department of Civil Affairs, Rui Xiebang of the Third Route Headquarters, Wang Weijun of the Department of Education, Ni Dexin of the Municipal Government, and Wu Yeshan of the County Reorganization Committee. Before the meeting started, the Japanese Consul Nishida Koichi secretly sent his police department's Japanese plainclothes detective Kaneko Sankyu, dressed in Chinese clothes, impersonated Chinese workers, and sneaked into the venue to gather information. He also held small flags and leaflets. Those who didn't know him regarded him as a Chinese patriotic man. In fact, Kaneko Sankyu has been in Jinan for many years. During the May Third Massacre, he led Japanese soldiers to brutally kill our compatriots. Many people in Jinan knew his face. Someone reported to a certain gentleman of the Provincial Reorganization Committee. The gentleman went forward to ask which group he belonged to. The Japanese claimed to be a worker. When asked in which factory he worked, he could not answer. The masses at the meeting believed that the Japanese dared to sneak into our citizens' assembly to gather information and advocated severe punishment. The Japanese saw that the situation was not good, so he scurried away. The meeting started at 9 o'clock. After Chairman Wang Yumin performed the etiquette, Wang Yumin reported on the purpose of the meeting, the facts of the National Humiliation Memorial Day, and the efforts that should be made in the future. Then Zhang Honglie, Director of the Department of Construction, Wen Chenglie, Mayor of Jinan, Wang Fangting, Director of the Department of Agriculture and Mines, Chen Weixin, Counselor of the Provincial Government, Wang Weijun, Chief of the First Section of the Department of Education, Rui Xiebang, Chief of the Propaganda Section of the Third Route Headquarters, and Yuan Changguo, a student of Zhengyi Middle School, delivered speeches one after another, all of which were extremely impassioned and慷慨. Jiawang Company Builds Jiahu Railway 77

The Route Runs From Jiawang to Huzhuang

Xuzhou Correspondence: The Jiawang Coal Mine in Northeast Xuzhou has been actively reorganized recently. The Huachang Company of the coal mine plans to build the Jiahu Railway in order to expand its business and alleviate the coal shortage for the public. The Jiawang Company used to transport coal to Huzhuang by ox cart several years ago. Huzhuang is a water terminal connecting Jinning in Western Shandong to Qingjiangpu in Northern Huaihe, which is very convenient for shipping by boat in peacetime. Now, the East China Company has sent an engineering specialist to start surveying. The measured route is planned to start from the Jiawang General Mine and end at the Huzhuang Ferry. A large amount of coal is transported from the General Mine to Huzhuang Ferry, and then transferred to Western Shandong and Northern Huaihe. It is predicted that the river is deep enough to carry ships of 20 tons, which is sufficient for transportation. General Manager Cheng of the company has recently negotiated a coal transportation contract with the Jinpu Railway authorities, which will be able to transport it in more than a month. According to the investigation, the mine currently produces 200 tons of coal per day, which is still a small amount. When the coal wells are completed and the old wells are repaired, a new No. 9 large well will be opened, and the coal mine will produce in large quantities, with water and land transportation to expand business. The mine also sent specialists to set up coal plants along the water and land lines to major towns and ports in the north and south for sales. In the future, the mine's output will probably further open up the Xuzhou's source of benefits. At the beginning of the operation, it was recognized to contribute to local public welfare donations, and it is also possible to allocate expenses for it. (11th)

In the recent four or five days, there has been continuous heavy rain and the weather is unusually cold. Silkworms eat wet leaves and suffer a lot of damage. Therefore, mulberry leaves have no market price, and early growers have already gone through three molts. In previous years, silkworm cocoon merchants were busy preparing for cocoon activities at this time. This year, seeing that the silkworms are not in good condition, they are very discouraged. Therefore, there is no news about the preparations for cocoon activities. The other day, silk factory merchant Cheng Bingruo hosted leaders of cocoon merchants in the county to discuss the cocoon activities this year, so as to avoid huge losses. After the heavy fog yesterday morning, the sky cleared up and the weather also warmed up. The future of sericulture may still have a glimmer of hope.

Over ten of Li's battalion soldiers were also killed or wounded. The captured bandit has now been beheaded and displayed as a warning, and the search for the remaining bandits continues.

Special Educational News

Further Discussion on Children's Reading Materials 90

(In response to Mr. Wu Yan'yin) Shang Zhongyi (II)

(II) Many proponents of fairy tales argue that children enjoy such stories and that they arouse their interest. However, we often hear children earnestly requesting "real" stories. Whether children truly enjoy imaginative reading materials can only be answered through long-term, systematic, and objective observation and precise experimentation. Empty talk and forceful arguments are of no use. Observations of this kind are still lacking, but practical experiments have indeed given us much knowledge. According to Dunn's recent detailed exploration, "imaginativeness" not only fails to arouse interest but even provokes slight aversion in boys. In addition, researchers who have conducted rigorous studies on reading interests, such as Terman, Zhao Deng (Joran), and Yu Er (UhI), all tell us that "imaginativeness" is by no means the best material for arousing interest, let alone the only method for stimulating fondness. Within the boundaries of not violating natural phenomena, there are many things that can arouse interest.

Taking a step back, let us assume that Dunn's, Zhao Deng's, and others' explorations contain errors or are not suitable for Chinese children. Let us further assume that "imaginativeness" can indeed arouse the interest of Chinese children. Can we then unconditionally follow this trend of interest? Do educators have a responsibility to shift preferences? Children like candy; should it be given without restraint? Toddlers want to possess everything they see; should this be suppressed? Therefore, even if "imaginativeness" could indeed arouse interest, it must be beneficial and harmless to children before it can be adopted. Moreover, we fundamentally doubt its ability to arouse interest. What's more, we also feel that its value is questionable and its dangers are manifold.

(III) Containing Lessons: Some people believe that the value of fairy tales lies in their implicit meaning between the lines. For the sake of discussion, let us put aside the question of whether containing lessons makes for good reading material and focus on the act of containing lessons itself. We feel that lessons based on facts and possible materials are likely to be more effective than lessons based on impossible fantasies. Fantastical allegories are sometimes difficult for even adults to understand, let alone children. Lessons based on impossible materials, which children know to be fictitious and fabricated, cannot inspire their confidence.

Summarizing the above three sections, we feel that the value of fairy tales is indeed questionable. The various reasons for maintaining their position in children's reading materials are insufficient. The so-called "inspiring imagination," "arousing interest," and "containing lessons" are all between having and not having, while reading materials that do not violate natural phenomena all "can have" the value that fairy tales "may or may not have," as well as "the dangers of fairy tales."

From a psychoanalytic point of view, fairy tales are most similar to dreamlike illusions and the fantasies of psychologically ill people. For adults to be too immersed in fantasy is detrimental to mental health, let alone children.

Children's sense of self is strong in their early years. Educators should assist them at this time, gradually enabling them to adapt to objective reality. During this process of proper adaptation, giving them material that contradicts the objective reality they are trying to adapt to can, in a passive sense, hinder the progress of their proper adaptation and, in an active sense, create a distorted adaptation. In the first step of this adaptation process, educators must be careful not to allow children to develop a fondness for leaving reality and immersing themselves in fantasy at an early age, lest they develop a tendency to seek satisfaction in fantasy.

Adults, with their experience and knowledge, often develop abnormal mental states when faced with the ruggedness of life's paths and the difficulty of dealing with reality, constructing self-deprecating psychologies such as "seeking satisfaction in fantasy," "everything is predetermined," "sour grapes," and "sweet lemons." Children, with their limited experience and knowledge, still need to adapt to this chaotic and complex adult society. Aiding and guiding them is still not enough to ensure they can cope with the real environment, lest they fall into abnormal mental states. How can we then dazzle them with fantasy and mislead them with the unreal?

The protagonists in fairy tales mostly achieve their goals through chance, magic, or lucky assistance, rarely creating happiness through direct effort and sincere striving. On this point alone, most fairy tales should be eliminated. Because our responsibility to children and society is to teach children to use sincere effort to seek the welfare of society and individuals, we must not encourage the kind of unearned happiness found in many fairy tales.

In short, the dangers of fairy tales can be summarized as follows: (1) They easily hinder children's progress in adapting to objective reality; (2) They easily lead to the habit of escaping from real life and fleeing into fantasy; (3) They easily lead to a tendency to seek satisfaction in fantasy or to pray for unearned gains; (4) They easily foster a sense of fear and aversion towards real life in children; (5) They easily lead to a process of bizarre and chaotic thinking.

(My Position) In the minds of most people, when children's reading materials are mentioned, fairy tales (including stories about gods and immortals, as well as other fantastical stories) are immediately associated with them, and children's reading materials and fairy tales are often confused. This is extremely unfortunate. In Zhongyi's battle against fairy tales, there are requests to fellow educators:

(1) It is essential to distinguish between the two terms "children's reading materials" and "fairy tales," and to recognize that fairy tales are only a tiny part of children's reading materials. Even if all fairy tales were banished, children's reading materials would still have a very broad and rich scope. Furthermore, regarding the analysis of the value and drawbacks of fairy tales, we can summarize it into two points: A. The value of fairy tales is indeed questionable; B. The subconscious dangers of fairy tales are indeed numerous. Is it permissible to use materials of questionable value and numerous dangers to occupy children's precious time? Instead of using this kind of reading material, why not use reading materials that have the value of fairy tales but without their dangers, based on facts and possible materials? Therefore, (2) It is essential to reduce the amount of time children spend on fairy tales to the bare minimum—allocating most of the time to reading materials that do not violate natural phenomena.

(3) Regarding the requirements for fairy tales themselves, we must greatly reduce the number of fairy tales and choose them with extra caution. (I will draft another article to discuss this kind of selection.) Only the first-class fairy tales that truly have artistic value and playful interest should be retained, such as Kipling's "The Elephant's Child" or Lofting's "Doctor Dolittle" (using only the first book). The motto for retention and selection is "Rather be short than shoddy."

(In response to Mr. Wu Yan'yin's questions)

Mr. Wu published his opinions on Zhongyi's lecture at the Children's Education Society in the Shenbao and Xinwenbao on the 29th and 30th of last month, raising five questions. Apart from points 1, 2, 3, and 4, which have natural answers in the above text, I will now take the opportunity to answer the remaining two:

Wu (Question): Should stories about gods and monsters be judged based on whether they are logical or illogical? Shang (Answer): Not only stories about gods and monsters, but all teaching materials and reading materials (except for a few humorous materials) should be judged based on whether they are logical or illogical. What right do adults have to give children materials that are "illogical"?

Wu (Question): What are the stories about animals that Mr. Shang mentioned that do not speak but only describe the animals' lives? Shang (Answer): From this question, it seems that Mr. Wu believes that without stories, there are no reading materials about animals. Zhongyi would sincerely like to introduce Jean-Henri Fabre's works to Mr. Wu. After reading them, perhaps this kind of question will no longer arise, and perhaps it will open up a new field in Mr. Wu's mind for children's reading materials. (The End)

National Assembly and National Education Lu Shaoji (II) 91

(VI) Emphasize Teacher Education: Teachers are the mothers of national education, or in other words, the foundation of the nation. They are the carriers of national culture. Whether we want to preserve national culture or develop national talent, we cannot do without their strength. This is what the education authorities should emphasize in teacher education. 1. Teacher training schools should be public in principle and should not be freely established. 2. Teacher education should be given special emphasis. The most suitable scientific education and the most rigorous physical and mental training must be used to cultivate teachers who are morally and academically sound as the main task.

(VII) Vigorously Implement Scientific Education: This is the current problem of Chinese education. If science does not flourish, then industry will not prosper, people's livelihoods will be impoverished, and the country's power will be weak. Furthermore, if science does not flourish, people's intelligence will not be enlightened, superstition will not be eliminated, and it will greatly hinder the progress of the revolution. Mr. Sun Yat-sen was aware of this, so he vigorously advocated scientific education (often advocating the import of scientific knowledge). Today, the National Government should put forward a sum of money specifically for the development of scientific education.

(VIII) Safeguard Educational Independence: This has two layers of meaning: 1. Independent educational funding (as stipulated by the Kuomintang government: "...increase educational funding and guarantee its independence"). All national educational funding should be collected, managed, and distributed by the education sector itself, and other agencies should not arbitrarily divert it. 2. Independent hiring rights for the education sector. From the Minister of Education to primary school and kindergarten teachers, there is considerable protection for their professional positions, and there are certain standards for the selection, appointment, transfer, demotion, dismissal, and removal of personnel. Among the two types of independence, "educational funding" is particularly important. If educational funding is not independent, there will be no educational fund, and there will be no hope for "saving the country through education."

Other points that national education should pay attention to in the future include promoting character education, implementing political education, emphasizing military education, improving rural education, implementing labor education, emphasizing commercial education, and improving the treatment of teachers and staff, as well as encouraging teachers and staff to engage in academic writing.

In short, the prevalence of national education is closely related to the strength or weakness of the country. I sincerely hope that this National Assembly can make detailed provisions in the law for the implementation of national education, so that all people in the country can be sound individuals, so as to promote constitutional government. (The End)

The draft budget for education expenditure in Anhui Province for the 20th year of the Republic has been prepared by the Department of Education and submitted to the provincial government for review. The total amount is over 2.39 million yuan, an increase of over 570,000 yuan compared to the 19th year. Shanghai Municipal Examination Regulations 96

The regulations for the Shanghai Municipal Higher General Examination Hall were finalized yesterday, totaling twelve articles: 1. All those taking the Shanghai Municipal Higher General Examination shall abide by these regulations. 2. Examinees shall enter the hall on time with their credentials according to the prescribed examination period and take their seats according to the assigned number. Those who do not bring their examination credentials shall not be allowed to enter the hall. 3. Examinees shall place their examination credentials on the table for each examination and shall not hide or deface them. 4. Examinees shall not bring books or notes other than writing instruments. 5. Examinees shall not rush to pass or transmit information. 6. Examinees shall not converse or inquire about examination questions in the examination hall. 7. After completing the answers to the examination questions, they shall submit the papers and leave the hall. 8. Examinees shall submit the papers on time, and late submissions will not be accepted. 9. Examinees who wish to leave the hall temporarily shall obtain the permission of the chief examiner or the supervising examiner. 11. Examinees who violate the above articles 3, 4, 5, 8, and 9 shall be ordered to leave the hall and shall not be allowed to continue the examination. 12. Any matters not covered shall be determined and announced by the chief examiner at any time.
