Free Talk

A Word or Two 108

— Long

One should naturally speak little about useless things. And even about things beneficial to oneself, one should speak little, because what is beneficial to oneself often causes harm to others.

A woman can only receive the love of the opposite sex in her youth. Therefore, in today's society, there are many sex maniacs in love, but no true love at all.

In the past, women were often afraid of being divorced by their husbands. Now, women are only afraid that their husbands are unwilling to divorce them.

Most good young people are caught in the web of love before leaving school. Before their studies are completed, they are already weary of life. Is this due to poor education or a bad society?

If you can understand that the money you suck from your compatriots is being used to manufacture guns and warships for future attacks on China, you will resist without being told to resist.

Today's students are in an environment of dancing and tea parties in the East and West. It is truly difficult to expect them to bury themselves in books and become talents to save the world from the violent sun.

Those who constantly use terms of endearment as a verbal tic are certainly not as devoted in their feelings as those who are taciturn.

The art of returning to youth does not exist in the world. Why are those who fight for power and profit so foolish?

If all countries do not quickly wake up from the delusion of dominating the world and continue to build weapons of mass destruction, there will be a day when humanity is wiped out.

Notes on a London Inspection 109

— Xu Shiqi

Among the famous cities of Europe, there are four. Rome is simple, solemn, and majestic, and rich in historical value. Paris, a flourishing art garden, uniquely releases wonders, and forms the center of modern culture. Berlin, cautious, dignified, and magnificent, represents the spirit of science. As for cities with a large population, holding the reins of the economic world, and flourishing in modern times through the development of industry and commerce, England is a giant.

London straddles both banks of the Thames River. The north is the city center, with towering buildings and endless mansions. The south bank is full of factories with thick smoke covering the sky. The population is over seven million, which can be described as a human beehive. This city has suffered two great catastrophes: the Great Plague in 1665 and the Great Fire in 1666. The entire city was reduced to ashes, and 70,000 people died. The English rebuilt London. Last summer, I had the opportunity to travel there. After getting off the train, I went directly to visit Ambassador Shi. The conversation was very pleasant, and he guided me to see the embassy and the room where Mr. Sun Yat-sen was detained during his ordeal in London. The room was on the third floor, barely able to accommodate the knees. There were iron bars outside the window, and the light was dim. I could imagine the feeling of being in an iron-barred cell. Ambassador Shi also introduced me to Sun Shifu, the embassy secretary, to be my guide, which was very touching.

The British Parliament is the origin of the world. It is located on the bank of the Thames River, covering an area of 30,000 square meters. The project took ten years and cost three million British pounds. It is one of the famous buildings in London. There are three towers standing majestically in the east and west. There are about hundreds of halls in the middle, magnificent and solemn. The walls are painted with portraits and sculptures of past kings. The auditorium has about 500 seats, while the number of members is 670. Those who do not occupy a seat when the majority is present have no right to speak. The British promote the creation of the parliamentary system to appeal to the world, but the fact that the chaos and irregularities are like this is quite strange.

Westminster Abbey was built in the seventh century and faces the Parliament. Successive kings ascended the throne and held coronation ceremonies here. The names of famous people and mausoleums are listed in the middle. The interaction of politics and religion can be seen here.

The British Museum is a Roman-style building, grand in scale. From the Stone Age to the present, the content is divided into treasures from various countries. In particular, there are countless ancient paintings, famous porcelain, jade seals, and classics from China, which were looted during the Boxer Rebellion. What is most heartbreaking is the display of various opium pipes, which are numerous and eye-catching. The British introduced drugs into China, but they do not realize it, instead mocking and belittling it. The intentions of the imperialists are also very dangerous.

There are two national art galleries. One collects paintings from the Middle Ages, masterpieces by outstanding artists such as Raphael Lebrun. The other was founded in 1890, when Tate personally donated his lifelong collection to the country, so it is also called the Tate Gallery. It displays paintings from recent centuries, new works such as Gauguin Matisse are also included. There are about 20 museums in London, and art galleries account for one-fifth of them. The scale and equipment are inferior to those of Paris.

Madame Tussaud's Exhibition was founded by Madame Tussaud, hence the name. Since 1802, almost all famous people from the government and the public have been listed. They are divided according to the changing times. The statue of Mr. Sun Yat-sen of China is also displayed in it. He is wearing a fur-collared coat, looking like a middle-aged man, but his cheeks are too full and not very similar. Great writers such as Shakespeare Dickens Scott Hugo Shaw and Bern, sitting and standing, are lifelike. The skill is amazing.

What is most noteworthy is that there are nearly two million unemployed workers in London, dressed in rags and squatting on the streets everywhere. Passing through its fields, there are thorns and weeds everywhere, and there is very little cultivation. Food and raw materials are all taken from the colonies, and there is a risk of insufficient supply.

A Record of a Farewell Spring Gathering 110

— Deng Chunshu

Half the cherries are as small as beans, and after nights of wind and rain, who knows how many flowers have fallen? The flowers are gradually fading, and the leaves are getting better. Bees are buzzing around a wisteria frame. The swallows also know that the spring is getting old, softly discussing how to hatch their chicks. Separated by the curtain, the sound is quiet, afraid that the paired birds will attract the laughter of the orioles. This is a spring evening poem by Mr. Yu Baoqing. I was wandering on Baiyun Creek, enjoying the spring in the beautiful pavilions. I only knew the beauty of the spring scenery, but I didn't know that the spring scenery was already fading. A few days ago, the members of the Mingshe Society gathered at Mr. Yu's Guangyutang for the third spring farewell gathering since Xinwei. The host was his son Lan Yu. Although there was heavy rain, twenty-eight people came from afar. Yao Gongjinqiu came from Jingkou, Xu Gongxiu from Qingpu, Yuan Mengbai from Shaoxing, Wang Xiucang from Xiaoshan, and I came from Wujin, borrowing the Xiling Seal Society to publish the second collection of my paintings and poems of scenic spots. Residents such as Chen Yitao from Haining, Gu Dingmei from Kuaiji, Li Zhonglian from Ji'an, Zhu Dake from Jiaxing, Wu Qinmu, Hu Jifan from Jixi, Chen Daolan from Chaozhou, Lu Anqin from Kunshan, Cao Shuhang from Wuxian, Zheng Zhian, and Huang Yingchan all arrived one after another. Everyone took out their spring farewell poems, and there were many wonderful works. The sound of chanting echoed the sound of rain. I also showed the horizontal scroll of the Mid-Autumn Festival painting with the fellows, the Yuanyang Lake Moon Viewing Picture. After the appreciation, the banquet was set up, but Zhu Guwei and Zheng Sucan could not come due to their deployment to the north. Sun Yusheng was prevented by rain, and they all sent letters of apology. So we entered the seat together, drinking wine and composing poems, almost forgetting what world we were in. Looking up, I saw a couplet written by Mr. Hu Shou hanging in the hall. The sentence said, "The spring atmosphere is perceived by poets, and sitting at night can deepen the understanding of painting." Reading it is like a pre-written gift for us to see the scenery. After madly chanting and tapping the beat, we got up after the wine was gone. Seeing the swords, spears, and halberds arranged in the courtyard, I asked in fear. I learned that Jian Yu was proficient in practice and had been practicing for many years. Not only is he a man of refined tastes, but his martial arts skills are truly a national weapon. He is worthy of his name Yuan Ying. After saying goodbye and leaving, the bell rang ten times. I listened to the rain in the hostel and recorded it. (No payment accepted)

Past and Present of Yangzhou Salt Merchants (Part 1) 111

— Shi Weng

The Chinese salt law was never inapplicable in the prosperous era of the Qing Dynasty. Over time, abuses arose, and it became increasingly decadent. Salt law reform is a real need. However, the dispute between the old and the new could not be resolved. Reading the Shen Bao on April 30, the reasons for delaying the implementation of the new salt law were mentioned. One was whether the tax collection on the spot without the intervention of salt merchants could reliably exceed the income of 130 million yuan per year. This statement is the most important. However, we common people do not want to argue too much. However, Yangzhou's prosperity has always been based on the salt industry. Last month, I passed through the Han River and took a look at the scenery. It was unusually desolate. I couldn't help but feel the changes between the past and the present.

Yangzhou is famous for its six dynasties. Since ancient times, there has been the poem "waist tied with a hundred thousand, spend it riding a crane to Yangzhou". It is true. Since the rise of the Salt Court, the salt merchants have built high platforms and wide mansions, constantly dancing and singing, sipping wine, and having beautiful women attend. A group of famous scholars and beauties competed to write poems. Those who could write poetry often had the sentence "a thousand families raise daughters, first teach them songs, ten acres of flowers are planted instead of fields." Its prosperity is indeed extreme. The officials below the Salt Court competed in splendor. Even the large flag outside the gate of the Salt Court earned a lot of silver every month. What else can be known? Now, a piece of wilderness has been turned into a sheep farm for a long time. After the restoration, I once passed by here and met an old woman in her seventies who said, "This was the old site of the Salt Court." Alas.

When Emperor Qianlong made his southern tour, it was extremely extravagant. The elegance was brilliant. Everything was perfect. The emperor casually said, "The scenery beside Xiaojin Mountain is extremely beautiful, but it lacks a pagoda." The salt merchant heard this and reported a pagoda in a few days. Or he casually said, "A bridge is missing in a certain place." The salt merchant heard this and built a bridge in a few days. This is still not surprising. What is even more surprising is that when I looked at the countryside in the spring, I suddenly saw four big characters arranged in the wheat field in the cauliflower bushes. The color was yellow and square. The words said "Long live the Emperor". Before the southern tour, the salt merchants had instructed the farmers to show them the shape of the characters and use rapeseed to plant them in the same style. It seemed natural. They only wanted to win the emperor's smile, and the amount spent was countless. Therefore, the name of the salt merchant was the best in the world. I once heard from the elders in Beijing that Emperor Qianlong said to the prince in jest when he returned to the palace, "It is better for you to be born in the family of a salt merchant in Yangzhou than to be born in the imperial family." Alas, how prosperous. Now, there are few carriages and horses under Pingshan Hall, and the willows and peach blossoms are falling by the Slender West Lake. In the winter of the seventh year of the Republic of China, I met a descendant of an old salt merchant begging on the road in Lvyang Village in the snowstorm. He had little money in his pocket. I only gave him eight hundred words. My heart trembled for it. The above is inevitable. Why can I bear this?

A Voyage around the Yellow Sea (1) 112

— Huang Yanpei

Time: March 19 - April 24, 1931

Itinerary: Qingdao, Dalian, Shenyang, Gyeongseong (Seoul) Korea, Busan, Tokyo, Hakone, Bikai (?), Seikyo (?), Osaka, Kobe, Nagasaki

Traveling is my nature. Perhaps it is my heredity. Because my father Jing loved to travel. Forty years ago, my father's footprints had already been all over the three major river basins of China.

Traveling is the most exciting thing, but there are also several conditions: (1) There must be suitable companions. (2) There must be a certain understanding of the places visited in advance. (3) There must be adequate physical strength and spirit. However, the excitement I speak of includes two aspects: laughter and crying. On March 19, I took the Dalian Maru from Shanghai. A flock of seagulls saw us off. From morning to night they did not leave. Three chapters on seagulls.

The blue sea is boundless. The white seagulls are in flocks. They linger at midday, going back and forth. Seagulls, you accompany me on a grand tour, sending me off for a thousand miles with earnestness. I have the same hobby as you, and I will roam the universe. Alas, alas, I know that high integrity is against the customs. Can a person not be as good as you?

The snowy waves are surging, and the boat is reading higher and higher. The seagulls are coming. I will invite you. Sometimes soaring freely in the air, and sometimes fluttering on the waves. Suddenly disappearing into the water, alarming the fish. Seagulls, you are the great enemy of the fish, and you still use your sharp beak to boast. I think of your need to survive, and I think of your empty stomach. Although there is not much food left, it is enough to feed your old age. Seagulls, seagulls, may you be auspicious phoenixes, not evil owls.

Seagulls, seagulls, you have a flock, and I also have a partner. This blue-clothed woman is my wife. That beard is white and beautiful. They are all my friends. Seagulls, if you have knowledge, I will introduce you to each other and shake hands. I hope that people and birds can be close to each other, and birds and fish can be close to each other. The harmony is a unity, and sincerity touches all things. All living things in the world should support each other and not betray each other. Keep my heart as calm as the unwavering waves, and may you live long and healthy.

The Storytelling Club

The Turning Point of the Hawthorne Detective Case (12) 113

— Cheng Xiaoqing

Hawthorne's composure has always been admired by me. Sometimes, no matter how his emotions change, he can keep them from showing on his face. At this time, his gaze was fixed, and his cheekbones were slightly flushed, showing the anger in his heart, which could not be suppressed. Zhang Baoquan also seemed to be hinted at, clenched his fists, and struck the table, as if expressing injustice for Hawthorne. I asked again, "Looking at it this way, this matter must not be accidental. What happened to you later?" Hawthorne said, "At that time, I had two understandings. First, maybe someone was deliberately playing a prank. Second, maybe someone wanted to play tricks in the Gao family, but they were afraid of me, so they deliberately transferred me away. So I rushed back to the Gao family and asked quietly, but nothing happened. I asked about you again. According to Pei Xian, he didn't even know when you left. So I became anxious, fearing that you might have been assassinated. I didn't know your whereabouts for a while, so I called your house first. You hadn't returned yet. I felt even more worried. I called my residence again. Shi Guicai told me that you were here. Now you haven't suffered much loss, but that necklace is another problem. Where is the necklace?" Hearing this, Zhang Baoquan had already opened the white cloth package on the table, took out the necklace, and handed it to Hawthorne with both hands. Hawthorne took it and looked at it, and exclaimed in surprise, "Alas, this thing is valuable. According to the current market price, it is worth five or six thousand -" When he said this, he suddenly held the necklace in his palm and paused as if weighing the weight of the circle. Then he walked to the electric light on the desk and brought the necklace closer to the light to take a closer look. A trace of a smile suddenly appeared on his always cold face. He let out a sound that was both admiring and mocking, saying, "What a pearl necklace. The price is worth more than thirty yuan." I couldn't help but jump up and say, "Is it fake?" Zhang Baoquan also blushed and replied, "Alas, my vision is really too bad." Hawthorne interjected, "You don't have to take the blame. This thing is really well made. You were also in a panic. Didn't I just see it wrong? Now let's not talk about empty words. How did this thing come about? What is the purpose of that person playing this trick? Let's all use our brains on this."

Grains: Clear Weather Causes Flour and Wheat to Both Weaken

Yu Hang Spring Silkworms All Suffer from Diarrhea 122

The silkworm season in various towns and villages of Yu Hang this year is quite prosperous, but the weather is not right. Most of the early silkworms failed, and the amount of late silkworms raised is still not small. Although the weather was cold after the silkworms woke up, with continuous cloudy and rainy days, farmers worked diligently day and night, and losses were still small. However, during the major sleep, there was heavy rain for two days and nights, causing the silkworms to eat wet leaves and all have diarrhea with yellow water. In recent days, there has been continuous heavy rain, and the weather has become even colder, and the silkworms are all suffering from diarrhea and dying. This year's silkworm harvest is likely to be hopeless.

All Wu Yuan Tea Production Reports Losses 125

The production volume of Wu Yi green tea is over 100,000 boxes annually, and it is the richest among the six tea-producing counties in Anhui Province. Among them, the production volume in the northern townships is the largest, followed by the eastern townships, and then the southwest. In the past, the new tea market started annually around the Beginning of Summer. Last year, the weather was earlier, but the mountain households still opened their gardens according to the season. Later, because they could not catch up with the harvest, there was mostly old grass, and buyers disliked the manufactured tea for being coarse and large, and no genuine goods could be taken, so they rejected it and did not purchase it. Therefore, many mountain households suffered from the disease of harvesting old grass late last year. No one asked, and there was nowhere to sell it, and the huge losses cannot be described in words. This year, each mountain household is afraid of repeating the same mistakes. Ten days before the Beginning of Summer, they have all chosen to pick early. According to the tea farmers in each village, each family's tea garden has been harvested and manufactured by half, and the quantity is less than six-tenths of previous years. The new tea produced by Shangbei Fengshan is similar to Mao Feng in its tenderness. The tea produced by Xiabei Longteng, Huangcun, and Jiacun does not need to be sifted and selected, and it is already like Fengmei. The tenderness of the shipment is rare since Wu Yi has tea. Therefore, each household estimates that the quantity of tea that has been harvested and has not been harvested has been reduced. Generally, it is necessary to discount 40%, and some have a sharp reduction in yield of 60%.

Fu Liang Later Batch Tea Prices Trend Downward 126

Fu Yi's new tea, according to the reduced number of tea firms this year, the mountain price should have been lower than in the past. Unexpectedly, the Qi Men tea firms are numerous and raise prices to compete for purchases. Although Fu Yi wants to suppress prices, it is difficult. They have to reluctantly follow suit and make purchases with pain. Therefore, the highest new price for the first grade of black tea has been raised to 90 yuan, and the second grade must also be 70 yuan. Various tea firms are trending madly in this market. Those who are cautious mostly temporarily suspend weighing and stop making purchases. In recent days, mountain households have been willing to reduce prices for sales because the new tea is fleeting and the tea itself is deteriorating daily compared to previous prices. The market in recent days seems to have turned sharply downward. The mountain price for each dan of the second and third grade tea purchased by each firm has already fallen from 90 yuan to around 50 yuan and 40 yuan. In addition, bandits are wandering in the tea-producing areas to rob them, and tea firms from far and near are all vigilant and dare not store much cash in the firm. There are occasional cases of weighing and purchasing as soon as possible to avoid danger. If the weather is not clear in the next few days, the price of tea will still tend to decline.

De Xing Tea Production is Expected to Increase 127

De Xing's tea production has always been abundant. Its tea land is adjacent to the Wu boundary, and the quality and taste are quite superior. Each year's new tea, in addition to the needs of the local tea firms, is also purchased by many Wu Yuan firms in De Xing. Last year, about 50% of the whole county's tea leaves were not harvested due to banditry, and the rural economy and income were greatly reduced. This year, the new tea in the county has also developed early. Mountain households are forced by livelihood. Although the Communists appear and disappear without constant pattern, the income from the annual sideline industry is a major source, and they are unwilling to abandon the benefits to the land. As in previous years, they allowed the old trees to remain unharvested. In recent days, most of the high-altitude tea in the areas of Xie Chong and Nan Chong Quan Qi in the east of the county has been formally harvested, and the tea quality is also more tender than in the past. Even the low-altitude tea near Kaihua Wannian is also being harvested. If there is no disturbance within two weeks, the amount of new tea produced this year may increase compared to last year.

The Price of Keemun Tea Is Unlikely to Fall 128

The initial batches of Keemun's "First Character Mountain" grade tea have been eagerly sought after by various firms, pushing prices to unprecedented highs. As is customary, prices for "Second" and "Third Character" teas tend to decline, but in recent days, fluctuating weather conditions, with alternating sunshine and rain, have slowed deliveries from the mountain farmers. Supply has been unable to meet demand, making it difficult for prices to drop immediately. Over the past two days, the weather has been sunny and favorable for drying and picking, resulting in superior deliveries. Nevertheless, prices have remained steady at 90 to 60 yuan across various markets. Cautious firms, recognizing the high costs involved and the slim chances of profit, have temporarily suspended weighing and procurement to avoid further losses. Some cite a lack of cash flow, hindering their ability to purchase in large quantities.

Piece Goods: Inland Merchants Gradually Begin Purchases

The piece goods trade showed signs of recovery yesterday, as inland merchants have been arriving in Shanghai in droves. Prices have stabilized, and the downward spiral of foreign yarn has ceased. Over a hundred deals were made for "Dian Qiu Xiang" fabric, indicating a potential shift from falling to rising prices. Sales of printed cotton fabrics have also been brisk, with "Shou Lao Qi Lu" selling for 3 candareens, 5 mace, 7 li and a half, "Jing An Si" for 2 candareens, 5 mace, 2 li and a half, and "Wo Long Gang" for 2 candareens, 5 mace, and a half. Inland merchants have been the most active buyers. Fine cloth is also gaining strength, with "Shi Le Niao" priced at 9 taels and 1 mace, and limited stock available. "Yue Yan" is priced at 9 taels and 9 mace. Printed cloth has been in high demand recently, with merchants from Qingdao and Hankou making consistent purchases, leading to a near exhaustion of supplies. "Shuang Tong Lu Chong" deep-patterned fabric sells for 5 taels, 3 mace and a half, and the new patterns of "Rong Hua Fu Gui" are mostly sold out. "Lun Chang" goods are also scarce in the market. Shanghai-dyed fabrics are more readily available, but prices are also quite high, exceeding 5 taels at the customs clearance. "Zhi Gong" woolen cloth, being out of season, experienced a price increase followed by a return to normal. Merchants from Hankou transported thirty to forty pieces of fine serge yesterday. The supply of "Zhi Gong" printed woolen cloth remains limited. "Qing Guan Jing" requires an asking price of 3 candareens and 8 mace and a half, while white crepe remains unchanged. Sales of imported cotton fabrics have been quite active, with blue-striped fabrics selling for around 3 candareens and 5 mace, and white-striped fabrics around 3 candareens and 4 mace.

North-South Goods: Sichuan Pickled Mustard Tuber Cheaper at Lower Grades

Sales of Sichuan pickled mustard tuber have remained sluggish across various regions, leading to a weak market, particularly for lower grades. The lowest grades are selling for as little as 23 yuan, while higher grades remain relatively stable, currently selling for 27 or 28 yuan. The abundance of lower-grade stock suggests the possibility of further price declines. However, considering the costs involved, all grades are currently operating at a loss, indicating that prices are unlikely to fall excessively.

The International Silver Conference Proposal

Proposed by the Chinese Representative

Representative Pei Advocates China Convening

However, countries seemed to be yielding to each other on the issue of initiating the conference, and some expressed doubts about China's leadership capabilities. Yesterday, a reporter from the Guowen News Agency specifically inquired about opinions from the banking community in Shanghai on this matter. The consensus was that China, being deeply affected by the high gold and low silver prices, should be well understood by all countries. However, the comment about whether our country can assume leadership should be heeded by the entire nation.

All representatives from the United Kingdom, the United States, France, and India expressed their support for the proposal to discuss silver prices. However, since this issue is only a matter for a part of the countries of the International Chamber of Commerce, another meeting must be convened, only if the countries concerned negotiate thoroughly. Therefore, this International Chamber of Commerce meeting failed to thoroughly discuss it. Our country's representative Mr. Pei has already reported the matter to Shanghai and intends to convene the meeting by our country after the closing of the International Chamber of Commerce. The location is also in our country, because our country also has an organization of the International Chamber of Commerce branch. To Relieve the Suffering of Shipping Merchants 133

Abolish the Inner Port Boat License and Yangtze River License

The Shanghai Shipping Association sent a letter to all member shipping companies yesterday, stating: "Regarding the case of domestic merchant ships sailing in the interior, there is a bad example of exchanging inner port licenses. This government decree is no different from self-binding, and shipping merchants have suffered for many years. The Association had previously submitted it to the National Transportation Conference and asked to abolish it. Although it was passed, it has not been implemented. Therefore, in March of this year, it was submitted to the Ministry of Communications to repeat the previous request, and then received instructions to consult the Ministry of Finance to cancel it, etc. After recording and printing the original submission and instructions, it was sent for inspection on April 3. Now, the Ministry of Communications instructs No. 699 to open, according to the request of the Association, and ordered to abolish the domestic merchant ships to receive the inner port special license, so as to facilitate shipping merchants, etc. It has been approved on April 3. Now, after consultation between the Ministry and the Ministry of Finance, in the future, domestic ships that have been given a ministry license can be exempted from giving boat licenses or river port special licenses and river licenses after going to the sea to open and inspect, so as to avoid complexity. In addition to amending the regulations on the registration and licensing of ships, it will be announced and implemented on the 2nd of this month, and it is hereby ordered to be informed. In view of this, the Association requested to abolish the inner port license, but now the boat license and Yangtze River license have been cancelled. The great intention of the Ministry to protect shipping merchants is more evident. The bondage and pain of decades have been lifted once and for all. In addition to waiting for the revised regulations on the registration and licensing of ships to be issued and delivered, it is hereby reported immediately, and I hope you will check it out." Jianghai Customs Announces New Rules for Cracking Down on Smuggling Taxes 134

Strict Regulations

When merchant ships transport goods, some unscrupulous crew members smuggle small packages and the goods are not listed in the hatch list. Not only does the shipping company suffer losses in water feet, but the customs also suffers from the impact of tax evasion. Last month, the Shanghai-Ningbo route had repeatedly cracked down on smuggling of large amounts of passenger and cargo goods, and one time found as many as thirteen barges. The local Jianghai Customs, in order to strictly prevent tax evasion, has specially formulated strict new rules and has been promulgated. For imported goods, the shipowners are responsible for reporting the hatch list. If there are any unlisted goods, they will be fined. The Jianghai Customs announced the strict new rules for preventing tax evasion, and selected important records: (1) Any merchant ship entering Chinese territorial waters or sailing in Chinese territorial waters shall have a hatch list signed by the shipowner, detailing the goods loaded, and submit it to the customs officer for inspection at any time. If it is found that there is no hatch list, the shipowner shall be fined no more than 500 taels of customs silver. (2) The hatch list shall contain the name, nationality, shipowner's name and the number of goods, as well as the number, mark and packaging style of each piece of goods. (3) The designated port of shipment and unloading. (4) Omitted (5) The goods carried on board (including transit goods), if there are any discrepancies with those not listed in the hatch list or listed in the list, the shipowner shall go to the customs within 24 hours after customs clearance to request correction, but only if the error is due to inadvertence or clerical error. However, goods not listed in the hatch list shall not be requested to be corrected if they have already been found by the customs. (6) If any goods not listed in the hatch list are found by the customs officers, the shipowner and the owner of the goods shall each be fined no more than 1,000 taels of customs silver, and the goods shall be confiscated. If the goods not listed in the manifest are hidden in a special way, and the customs officers find that the shipowner has done his duty, carefully supervised, and did not know the hiding of private goods, the penalty may be reduced. If there are several packages of goods packed in one piece, and the words "several packages packed together" are not noted, it shall be deemed as not listed in the hatch list. (7) If goods listed in the hatch list are found by the customs not to be among the goods carried on the ship, and the shipowner cannot point out and provide solid evidence that the missing goods were loaded at the original port of departure or unloaded in transit, the shipowner shall be fined no more than 500 taels of customs silver for each piece of goods. (8) Any merchant ship exporting without the permission of the customs shall be fined 1,000 taels of customs silver. (9) Warships, yachts and river-leading ships are not managed by these rules.

Lin Kanghou's Views on Recovering the Kailuan Mines 138

Yesterday, someone met with Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce of the Republic of China, and asked about the Kailuan Mines recovery case. Public clamor is very high at the moment. In the end, are there any concrete measures from all parties, and can it become a reality, etc. According to Lin's personal observation, this issue is extremely complicated and does not seem to be resolved in a short time. It is especially inappropriate to discuss it together with the current dispute between Kailuan and the Railway Bureau. Mr. Lin's intention is that in the past, many Chinese people thought that the use of foreign capital was harmful to the country. However, based on the facts, it does not seem to be the case. Taking the two organizations involved in the dispute this time as an example, the Beining Road was also built with foreign investment, with an annual interest rate of 5%, and an annual surplus of several million yuan. Kailuan Mine produced more than 5.5 million tons of coal last year, and the total selling price should be around 60 million yuan. However, the shareholders of Kaiping, many of whom are Chinese, received only more than 3 million yuan. In addition to being used for purchasing materials and machinery, and paying foreign salaries, the rest of the money is obtained by Chinese people. More than 40,000 workers rely on the mine for a living, and their monthly wages should be more than one million, which is also an important issue for the livelihood of workers. Nowadays, countries all over the world invest in each other's industries. If our country wants to revitalize its industry without foreign capital, it may not be easy to have large-scale development in a short period of time. Recently, Deputy Commander Zhang sent Zou Zuohua, the Commissioner for Xing'an Reclamation, to go abroad to raise foreign capital to develop the resources of Northeast China, which is the intention. I previously met with Lu Qisheng, the standing committee member of the Coal Industry Association, and talked about recovering the Kailuan Coal Mine. He said that people in the association are actively proceeding and intend to petition the authorities to issue 10 million yuan in public bonds to borrow cash from banks at a 70% discount. Fellow traders only need to raise 3 million yuan in cash to prepare for the recovery. I extremely agree with the recovery of the mine, but the recovery procedure may not be so simple. According to reports, the redemption price is 70 million yuan or 100 million yuan. Regardless of the amount of money needed, it will definitely not be resolved in a short time. At present, Kailuan coal cannot be transported south, and factories that need it everywhere will inevitably suffer. In short, recovery and suspension of operations are absolutely two separate matters, and those who talk about recovery now seem to be aimed at prolonging the suspension of operations, and the losses of general users and industry have not been taken into account at all. The output of mines that are completely Chinese-owned is limited, and transportation is also difficult. After Kailuan is shut down, its sales will definitely not be compensated by mines run by Chinese people. Those who replace it are being taken over by others. This should be paid attention to by Chinese people.

Finance Bureau Takes Over Slaughter Tax 144

The City Chamber of Commerce Drafts Three Suggestions for Mediation

Pigs are Allowed to be Released on Credit After Slaughter

The Meat Industry Discusses Follow-up Measures Today

The fresh meat industry was taken over by the Finance Bureau to receive the slaughter tax of Shangbao II counties and began to levy it on May 1. Fresh pigs must be counted and charged after slaughter, which led to shipping disputes. The industry petitioned the City Chamber of Commerce to mediate, and the City Chamber of Commerce drafted opinions: (1) The tax from the 1st to the 15th of this month, within half a month, will be paid uniformly when the entire case is resolved in the future, and the Chamber of Commerce will be responsible for it. (2) The fresh pigs slaughtered within the period up to the 15th of this month shall be counted temporarily and allowed to pass unhindered without detention. (3) The City Chamber of Commerce will convene the industry before the 15th to properly plan measures and consult with the Finance Bureau for resolution. As for the pigs that have been slaughtered and detained, they should all be released first to avoid spoilage. The above three items have been sent to the Finance Bureau by the Association. According to the staff of the Finance Bureau, the two counties of Shangbao have been incorporated into the urban area, and the slaughter tax is approved by the Jiangsu Education Fund Management Office to be transferred to the city for management, and funds are allocated monthly to subsidize education expenses. The Bureau followed the instructions of the Municipal Government and issued tax tickets on May 1 and implemented the levy, still according to the old tax rate. Each pig is taxed at 39 cents, and each sheep is taxed at 20 cents. It is not a new tax, and it does not increase any burden on meat merchants. In addition, direct collection is the principle of sorting out taxes, but after repeated persuasion, all meat merchants use the excuse of waiting for the association to resolve the matter, and do not buy tax tickets. I don't know what the intention is. In order to implement the laws and regulations, the Bureau sent personnel to the slaughterhouse on the 9th to carry tax tickets to persuade them to purchase on the spot, so that they could count the number of animals and cut corners to facilitate them. However, they still did not comply, so they checked the regulations and did not allow the slaughtered pigs to leave the factory. Now that the tax has been taken over by the City Chamber of Commerce, the tax collection offices have been instructed to temporarily count the number of animals and allow the pigs to be released, and the City Chamber of Commerce has been informed to convene a meeting to give detailed instructions and order them to purchase slaughter tax tickets and wait for inspection from May 16. The tax for the first half of the month should be paid as soon as possible. If they fail to comply after the deadline, they will still be dealt with according to the regulations. It is heard that the meat industry will convene a general meeting at 3:00 pm today to discuss follow-up measures for the slaughter tax.

Egg Industry Associations Telegraph Request to Reduce Tax Rates 146

Telegram to the Ministry of Finance

The Shanghai Egg Industry Association telegraphed the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating: "We have recently read in the Shen Bao the new export tax rates issued by your ministry. Dried eggs are taxed at 4.5 taels per dan for export, and wet eggs at 1.5 taels per dan. The original tax rate was 1.5 taels per dan for dried eggs, plus a surtax of 7.5 fen, totaling no more than 2.25 taels. Wet eggs were taxed at 2.25 li per dan, plus a surtax of 1.125 fen, totaling no more than 3.375 fen. Now, the surtax has been eliminated, but the basic tax has increased by three to four times, which is alarming. According to the recent selling prices of various egg products, egg white is 100 taels per dan (equivalent to only 90 taels on the customs scale, including customs duties; the following is similar), dried yolk is 55 taels, machine-made dried yolk (commonly known as "flying yolk") is 60 taels, dried egg powder (containing both yolk and white) is 70 taels, machine-made dried egg powder is 75 taels, and wet yolk is 23 taels. Among these, machine-made dried yolk and machine-made dried egg powder should be exempted from taxation according to the general practice for exporting machine-made products. All other products are cooked goods and should not be treated the same as raw goods such as fresh eggs and frozen eggs. At a time when the government is promoting foreign trade and encouraging the export of cooked goods, it should also specifically reduce taxes to protect domestic industries. However, the reality is the opposite. Comparing the selling prices of various goods with the new tax rates, the tax burden is almost 10% of the value, which is unbearable for businesses with already meager profits. The annual export volume of egg yolk and white in our country is no less than that of silk and tea, and the difficulties in operating the business are even greater than those of the silk and tea industries. Recently, it has also been affected by the United States' increasing import tariffs, and the future of the business is precarious. If we do not receive the government's consideration and support, we fear that this fledgling industry, even if it tries hard to maintain itself, will be on the verge of extinction. The association has carefully examined the situation and cannot remain silent. Therefore, we urgently request your excellency to promptly revise the tax rates, reduce or exempt them separately, and provide a written reply for compliance. This would be a virtuous and convenient measure."

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Petitions for Relief from Difficulties in Various Industries 147

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday submitted a petition to the Bureau of Social Affairs for transmittal to the Ministry of Industry, stating that it was replying to an official matter. On February 27th, the bureau issued Instruction No. 7044, based on Instruction No. 1215 from the Ministry of Industry, instructing the chamber to investigate the recent facts and difficulties of various industries and methods of relief, in accordance with the resolutions of the proposals by Xu Peihuang and Wu Jian at the industrial and commercial conference. The chamber was instructed to avoid empty talk and biases and to compile a report. The chamber then sent letters to various industries to investigate and reply. Now, regarding the replies received from various industries, we have selected those that avoid empty talk and biases and listed them as follows: (1) Flour mills request two items: (A) The special tax subsidy should be increased. The cost of setting up factories in Shanghai is particularly high, and the wages are very large. The wheat needed is transported to Shanghai from other ports, which is expensive and results in significant losses. Therefore, the cost is more expensive than in the inland. Even if the special tax subsidy cannot be raised compared to inland flour mills, it should be the same as inland flour mills. (B) Heavy tariffs should be imposed on imported flour, and Chinese flour should be completely exempt from export tariffs. The price of imported flour from the Americas and Australia is two or three qian lower per bag than Chinese flour and is sold well in Shenyang, Tianjin, and major ports in Southeast Asia. Chinese flour has almost no place to compete. Imported flour has no tariffs and only a special tax of one jiao per bag. It is urgent to consider imposing import tariffs or anti-dumping duties to resist it. As for Chinese flour exported overseas, the special tax was previously reduced by five fen, but now it is taxed at one jiao, which hinders development. It should be exempted to reduce costs and protect it. (2) The brick and tile industry requests one item: (C) Prohibit "bailala" brick and tile brokers from obtaining licenses and paying taxes to be able to open businesses. Brick and tile shops have various expenses, including partners' salaries, and the commissions earned are limited. However, cunning individuals cleverly establish "bailala" broker names to solicit business. These people do not obtain licenses and do not need to rent houses or hire partners. Therefore, although the construction industry in Shanghai has been flourishing in recent years, the brick and tile industry has not been doing well and has been closing down one after another, which is due to the influence of "bailala". It should be requested that the Public Security Bureau issue a strict prohibition order, and that the water and land police teams be instructed to send "bailala" brokers to be investigated according to law. At the same time, the association should be allowed to report and assist in identifying them at any time, which would benefit both national taxes and commerce. (3) The coal industry requests two items: (D) Request the National Government to order the entire country not to prohibit people from setting off firecrackers during non-martial law periods. Recently, public security bureaus in various places have been prohibiting the setting off of firecrackers for no reason, which would completely eliminate the industry. It is proposed to change this to non-martial law periods, which are not subject to the prohibition, in order to maintain it. (E) Abolish the saltpeter and sulfur trading system and allow the industry to apply for passports to purchase them. Since the establishment of the saltpeter and sulfur bureau, the prices of public sales have been repeatedly raised, and the cost is increasing day by day, which hinders the sales of the industry. It is not enough to save it unless licenses are obtained for self-purchase. The above are the circumstances of the various industries' requests for relief from difficulties. We have summarized them for your bureau's review. It would be a great convenience to transmit the report.

Repairing the Shihu Dang Railway This Morning 148

All Trains Temporarily Suspended

The Engineering Department of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway has found that the steel rail sleepers laid between Fengjing and Shihu Dang (approximately twenty li) have been in disrepair for many years and are inevitably rotten. In order to ensure the safety of train operations, all steel rail wood in the area will be replaced. Work is scheduled to begin at 4:30 AM this morning and end at 8:30 AM. During this repair work, there is a risk of train accidents. Therefore, all stations were notified yesterday that the No. 405 freight train departing from the Zhabei station should stop at Fengjing and pass through at 8:30 AM. Other unscheduled inbound trains should also be detained at Fengjing to avoid danger. Please be informed.

Airline Expands Postal Routes 149

Planning Shanghai-Chongqing and Shanghai-Guangdong Routes

Reduced Postage Rates for Beijing-Ping Line

China National Aviation Corporation has recently expanded its business and developed air routes to complete its original national route plan. It has decided to launch direct flights between Shanghai and Chongqing in mid-July and between Shanghai and Guangdong in early August, carrying only mail. Effective immediately, postage rates for Beijing-Ping airmail will be uniformly set at 15 cents for items within 20 centimeters. The news received yesterday is recorded as follows:

Beijing-Ping Line Postage Rates: The Beijing-Ping Line has been operating every morning (except for one day of suspension per week) for almost a month. The company is currently focusing on postal transport. In one or two months, it plans to add passenger transport. Mail transported on the Beijing-Ping Line is carried by the Shanghai-Yichang direct flight to Nanjing Ming Palace every morning, where it is unloaded and transferred to the Beijing-Ping flight for transport to various stations along the line. Tianjin mail is transported to Beijing by the Beijing-Pukou Railway on the same day and then delivered to various stations the next morning. However, the flights between the two lines (Beijing-Ping and Hankou-Yichang) are sometimes delayed due to bad weather. Each station is notified by radio and takes off after a short delay. Therefore, Shanghai flights sometimes fail to arrive in Beijing in time to hand over mail to the Beijing-Ping flight, which then takes off north. Currently, in order to achieve speed, the company will transport mail from Shanghai to the Beijing-Ping line to the capital by the Beijing-Ping day and night express train, and then transfer it to the northbound flight to Beijing and Tianjin. Tianjin mail will be transported to Tianjin by the Beijing-Pukou train on the same day, eliminating any delays. According to the company's original plan, postage for mail over 1,000 kilometers was 3 jiao per 20 centimeters. The company has now agreed with the postal authorities that, effective immediately, postage for all stations on the Beijing-Ping line will be uniformly set at 15 jiao, regardless of distance.

Shanghai-Chongqing Line Planning: The direct Shanghai-Chongqing line, which is being planned, will be launched in mid-July. The aircraft ordered from the United States will arrive in Shanghai in a month. Airports in Wanxian and Chongqing have been surveyed and appropriate locations have been determined. Radio equipment will soon be transported for installation.

Continuing to Establish Shanghai-Guangdong Line: The company plans to launch the Shanghai-Guangdong line in early August. In the future, it will fly along the coast, taking off from Shanghai and passing through Ningbo, Wenzhou, Fuzhou, Xiamen, Shantou, Hong Kong, and other stations before flying to Guangzhou. Floating pontoons will be placed along the coast for aircraft to stop and land. The company also telegraphed the American Sikorsky Aircraft Manufacturing Company to purchase two more seaplanes in order to achieve the goal of launching flights to all stations in the plan on schedule, which will depend on the environment.

Tianjin Station Awaiting Survey: The French barracks near the Tianjin East Bureau's aircraft station is obstructing operations, and aircraft cannot land. However, negotiations are underway, as it is the responsibility of the diplomatic sector. The company is an operating agency. Negotiation is one thing, and station establishment and flight operation are another. Therefore, it has been decided to entrust the Tianjin office to find a better location to build the Tianjin station, which will benefit airmail transport.

Japanese Trade with China in April 150

The Japanese Commercial Counselor's Office in Shanghai recently received a telegram from Japan stating that the value of goods exported from Japan's six major commercial ports to China in April totaled 21 million Japanese yen, exceeding the total value of goods imported from China by 4 million Japanese yen. The total value of Japan's exports in April was 81 million Japanese yen, which was 45 million Japanese yen less than the total value of imports. Since New Year's Day, Japan's trade deficit has reached 82 million Japanese yen.

Request to Stop Foreigners from Establishing Factories in China 151

The National Products Maintenance Association Telegraphs a Request to the National Government and Party Headquarters

The China National Products Maintenance Association sent a communication to the National Government Central Party Headquarters, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Industry, and the Ministry of Culture, stating: "Respectfully submitted, on April 6th, we sent a special telegram requesting measures to prevent foreigners from establishing factories in China. We believe this matter is of great importance and requires the convening of all Shanghai national product industry and commerce circles to conduct a thorough discussion, gather opinions, and jointly vote to contribute to the government's request for adoption and implementation. Therefore, on the 20th of last month, we convened the All Shanghai National Products Industry and Commerce Representative Assembly. After detailed discussions by the representatives, the following six points were resolved: (1) Request the National Government to promptly formulate special regulations for the registration of foreigners establishing factories in China. For foreign factories that have already been established, in addition to ordering them to register according to law, heavy taxes should be levied on their products, business taxes, and anti-dumping duties. (2) Request the Ministry of Industry to effectively implement the National Products Encouragement Law and provide strong support for its development. (3) Request the Ministry of Finance to reduce or exempt taxes on national products to ease their burden. (4) Request the National Government Central Party Headquarters to instruct party and government officials at all levels to use national products and intensify the promotion of national products. (5) Request the Ministry of Industry to instruct administrative officials at all trading ports to strictly prohibit foreigners from secretly transporting workers from their countries to China to work, so as to avoid seizing the livelihoods of Chinese workers, especially paying attention to Russia and Japan. (6) Request the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to notify the governments of all countries to instruct their merchants to mark the nationality, factory name, and location on their products; otherwise, once discovered, they will be confiscated or heavily fined. The above points are currently the most urgent and necessary measures. We request the government to adopt and implement them to consolidate people's livelihoods and protect national rights. Recorded in the minutes, in addition to gathering various groups to work together, promote public awareness, encourage compatriots to love national products, and reject foreign goods, we should follow the resolution and respectfully submit the report. We earnestly request that you review and approve the implementation. We are anxiously awaiting your command, and we respectfully await your instructions. This would be a virtuous and convenient measure. Standing Committee Members of the China National Products Maintenance Association, Wang Jie'an, Wang Moyi, and Wang Hanqi, bow in truth."

Resolution of Labor Dispute at Far Eastern Sawmill 152

Workers Have Resumed Work

Over five hundred workers at the American-owned Far Eastern Sawmill in western Shanghai went on strike to demand the restoration of their original working hours. The day before yesterday, Gu Bingyuan from the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs went to mediate and obtained the consent of the foreman, Mr. Bell, and worker representative Wu Dalun to the resolution plan: (1) All workers will immediately return to work. (2) All workers will work in shifts, with each shift working at least four days per week. (3) By June 1st, if the factory can find a way to rent neighboring land for use as a warehouse, the non-shift system will be restored. Therefore, all workers have returned to work immediately.

Local News Two

Sudden Wealth Creates Trouble 153

Poor Friends Agree to Extort

Problems Indeed Arise

Confiscated Jewelry and Large Sums of Money

Seemingly Related to Gold Bar Robbery

Wang Lanlin, who had carried gold bars worth over 5,000 yuan, was robbed at the Jardine Wharf in Yangshupu on October 23rd of last winter. Half a year has passed, but the case has not yet been solved. Recently, Wang Hanqing, a native of Henan residing at No. 177 Miller Road, suddenly became rich. Ma Wenliang, a watchman at the Baoxing Silver Shop on East-West Huade Road, a fellow villager and longtime acquaintance of Wang, as well as Zhu Mutang from Tianjin and Zhou Deju from Shandong, all suspected that his wealth was not obtained legitimately. They all believed that it would be fine to extort from this kind of ill-gotten wealth. If he was willing to share the spoils, they would mutually conceal it; otherwise, they would rather perish together. On the 18th of last month, they gathered Wang Jinpeng and went to Wang's house to demand 300 yuan. Wang's wife, Zhang, refused to give them a single penny, which led to an argument. At that time, Wang's brother, Fuyou, his sister-in-law, Yang, and his son, Cuibao, all quarreled with them. Wang immediately reported to the Hongkou police station, and detectives Yang Zhaoqing and Liu Yongxiang rushed to investigate and arrest them. Ma and Wang Jinpeng had already fled. Only Zhu and Zhou were caught, and they confessed the details of the extortion. The detectives then re-entered Wang's house and, as expected, found 550 yuan in cash and a draft for 7,000 yuan in the pockets, waists, and shoes of the two women, Zhang and Yang, and Cuibao. In addition, they found 16 pieces of jewelry, including gold bracelets, gold necklaces, and gold rings. Wang and his brothers, their wives, and their son, a family of five, were all arrested. They then went to the Baoxing Silver Shop and arrested Ma. Wang Jinpeng was not arrested until the day before yesterday in a house at No. 498 Guangdong Road. Yesterday morning, they were taken to the Special District Local Court for investigation. The police lawyer stated that the gold bar robbery case still needed to be investigated and requested a postponement of the hearing. Wang Jinpeng then confessed that Ma Wenliang and Wang Hanqing were fellow villagers, and Ma knew that Wang had robbed a large amount of wealth, so he invited everyone to extort 300 yuan from Wang. Judge Feng subsequently ordered the defendants to be detained separately pending further investigation.

Rickshaw Boat Registration Disturbance in Wusong 154

Conflict Caused by Misunderstanding

Assault Caused by Conflict

Eighteen North Sea dried fish boats arrived in Wusong yesterday morning, sixteen of which were sold by the Cui Sheng Fish Company and two by the Baofeng Fish Company. As these fish boats were arriving in Wusong for the first time, they had not gone through registration procedures. The patrol boat of the Bureau of Public Utilities' Ship Affairs Office went to the river in the morning and summoned the boatmen (one person per boat) to the bureau. They were detained until after noon, around 12:00 PM, without being released. The fish boats all contacted Cui Sheng for negotiation. The company sent representatives, along with Jiang Rusong, the owner of the Xietai tax reporting agency, to the bureau to discuss having the fish company pay the registration fee (3 yuan per boat, plus a daily donation of 2.16 yuan) and monthly donation. The bureau refused and insisted that, according to the regulations, each boat had to send one boatman to the bureau to inquire about the boat's name, pay the donation, and then be issued a license plate and a lamp before the boatmen would be released. However, this procedure took a long time, so the boatmen believed that they were being deliberately detained, which caused great dissatisfaction. Unexpectedly, Director Yang of the bureau went to the boats a second time in the afternoon and summoned the boatmen. At that time, the boatmen thought that the boat donation had already been paid by the fish company, so why were they being arrested again? The misunderstanding arose from this, and because the boats were eager to open their holds and sell fish, a conflict broke out, resulting in violence. Director Yang, seeing that the situation was not good, swam away and rushed to the 4th Water Patrol Division, ordering the police to arrest them immediately. The water patrols saw that the boatmen were not on the boats, so they rushed to the Cui Sheng Fish Company and arrested the injured boatmen Wang Jinyu, Lü Wanzhi, Lü Wanmao, and Lü Wancheng, causing great injustice to all the boatmen and all the fish merchants in Wusong Town. They all wanted to go to the bureau to question them. After Zheng Shushan, the president of the Chamber of Commerce, learned of the matter, he feared that it would lead to a town-wide fish merchant strike. He went to the 4th Water Patrol Division to bail out the four injured boatmen and sent them to the Seaside Public Hospital for treatment. He also discussed a proper solution with Director Yang, and the strike was averted. Mediation is currently underway.

Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau Compiles Report on the Order of Household Registration Changes 155

The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau believes that most citizens still have a rudimentary understanding of household registration change reports. Therefore, it has recently compiled an illustrated explanation that is distributed to households and posted in various places. The diagram shows the following: (1) Report within three days of birth. (2) Report on the day of death. After receiving the report, the precinct will issue a coffin transport certificate, burial certificate, and permit. After burial, the burial permit must be submitted. (3) Report three days before moving out. After receiving the report, the precinct will issue a move-out certificate. (4) Report within three days of moving in. (5) Report on the day of adoption. (6) Report three days before moving (within the city). After receiving the report, the precinct will issue a move certificate. After moving, the move certificate must be submitted. (7) Report within three days of inheritance. (8) Report three days before marriage. After receiving the report, the precinct will issue a marriage certificate. After marriage, the marriage certificate must be submitted. In addition to the above eight items, there are three items that must be reported based on the situation in this city, which are recorded on the left: (A) Visitors: If relatives and friends of residents come from outside the city or family members and friends go out and stay temporarily, if they leave Shanghai or return to Shanghai within three days, they can be exempted from reporting. If it is more than three days, they must explain the reason and submit a written report. (B) Separation: If a father, son, uncle, nephew, brother, or sibling of a resident divides the family, regardless of whether they live in the same household or move to another household, they must report three days in advance. If they live within the jurisdiction of the city, they must also report to the new precinct three days after moving, surrender the move certificate, and exchange it for an investigation certificate. (C) Missing: If a family member or employee of a resident leaves home and their whereabouts are unknown, they must report within three days. If a citizen commits one of the above-mentioned circumstances and does not report it, once discovered, they will be subject to detention for up to ten days or a fine of up to ten yuan. If they refuse to be investigated during a spot check or intentionally make a false report, they will be subject to a fine of one yuan or more and five yuan or less. If they obstruct the Public Security Bureau's investigation, they will be subject to detention for five days or more and one month or less, or a fine of five yuan or more and thirty yuan or less. However, the punishment for this obstructing behavior will be decided by the Municipal Public Security Bureau. All other matters will be enforced by the chief of the police district.

More Rickshaws in the City 156

Registered Number… 3,565 Vehicles

Subtracting the Actual Number… 1,477 Vehicles

The original number of rickshaws (commonly known as "yellow bags") operating in the city, including Shanghai South and Zhabei, was 4,500 in Shanghai South and 2,900 in Zhabei, totaling 7,400. Previously, due to citizens' requests for an increase in the number of vehicles, the Municipal Government approved an expansion to 10,000 vehicles, excluding special zones. The Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities and the Bureau of Finance discussed reserving 1,000 vehicles for Pudong and 200 vehicles for Wusong and the three-wheeled rickshaws that should be eliminated, with 1,400 vehicles being the actual number to be increased. Registration began on April 11 and ended on April 25. As a result, a total of 488 households registered 3,565 vehicles, exceeding the quota of 1,400 vehicles by 2,165 vehicles. The Municipal Government then sent personnel to review and reduce the number of vehicles along with the two bureaus of public utilities and finance. The regulations are as follows: (1) Households registering one or two vehicles will not be reduced. (2) Households registering three to ten vehicles will each be calculated at one-half, and households with a remainder of one vehicle after the reduction will also be calculated as two vehicles. For example, three vehicles will be calculated as two vehicles, and seven vehicles will be calculated as four vehicles. (3) Households registering eleven to twenty vehicles will each be calculated at one-third, and households with a remainder of two vehicles after the reduction will also be calculated as three vehicles. For example, eleven vehicles will be calculated as four vehicles, and fourteen vehicles will be calculated as five vehicles. (4) Households registering twenty-one to two hundred vehicles will each be calculated at one-fourth, and households with a remainder of two or three vehicles after the reduction will also be calculated as four vehicles. For example, twenty-two vehicles will be calculated as six vehicles, and thirty-four vehicles will be calculated as nine vehicles. According to the above methods, the actual number of vehicles reduced is 1,477, still exceeding the quota by 77 vehicles, which will be made up from the 1,000 vehicles reserved for Pudong. The two bureaus have jointly announced to the registered vehicle dealers that, starting from May 20, they should go to the Bureau of Public Utilities to obtain permits according to the number of vehicles they are entitled to, and manufacture the vehicles and report them for inspection in accordance with the regulations. The guarantee deposits for the number of vehicles reduced can be returned to the Bureau of Finance with the receipts previously issued.

Rickshaws in the French Concession 157

Association Requests Improvement of Donation Certificates

The Shanghai Rickshaw Association sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating: "According to a report from member Li Chunhe, the donation certificates issued by the French Municipal Council are not durable. Often, before the end of the month, the paper and the lead sheet separate, leaving a torn and incomplete certificate. Even if the paper is eroded by wind and rain and nothing is left, the license number can be checked on the aluminum sheet. However, most patrolling constables, knowing this is the case, deliberately 'check' and, seeing the above situation, immediately detain them, accusing them of 'smuggling' or 'stealing'. Foreigners, unaware of the facts, fine them at least five yuan or detain them at the police station. Even if they pay the donation for a new certificate, they are still punished. Such heavy treatment disregards right and wrong and disregards the difficulties of merchants. We request that you negotiate on reasonable grounds.' The association believes that donation certificates are valid for one month, and if the certificate loses its effectiveness within one month due to circumstances beyond one's control, the party responsible for the donation should find a way to remedy it. In any case, the donor is already unfortunate and should not be made to suffer any further losses. This is only reasonable. There are three types of rickshaw licenses in this city: Chinese, British, and French. The French license has the worst pasting quality. Before the expiration of the term, it wrinkles, tears, and becomes unrecognizable. Rickshaw merchants have repeatedly requested improvements, but they remain corrupt and the abuses continue. Foreigners blindly listen to the police's one-sided account and arbitrarily interfere, while the police fan the flames and take the opportunity to show their diligence and merit. Our rickshaw industry has dared to be angry but not to speak for a long time. Now that we have received this report, we respectfully request your association to forward it to the French authorities, requesting that they promptly improve the pasting process of rickshaw licenses for business purposes and, before a practical improvement is made, stop the illegal treatment of impounding vehicles and fining them in order to satisfy public opinion and relieve merchants' difficulties. We are eagerly awaiting your command."

Medical Doctor Li Zhongkang Returns Home 160

Dr. Li Zhongkang, originally named Li Shanjun, is a native of Nanxun, Wuxing, Zhejiang. He graduated from the Medical Department of Shanghai Tongji University in 1925. He served as a physician in the Internal Medicine, Dermatology, and Ophthalmology departments of the Baokang Hospital on Baker Road. In 1928, he went to Germany via Siberia to study further. The following year, the University of Rostock in Germany awarded him a doctorate in medicine. He then went to Berlin and worked as a doctor in the Internal Medicine Department of the University Hospital. He was then transferred to Vienna, Austria, to study at a specialist hospital for gastrointestinal diseases. Last year, he went to the Pediatrics Department of Hamburg University Hospital and worked as a doctor. He was highly praised by the Dean of the Hospital, who gave him a letter of recommendation. Mr. Li has now returned to Shanghai and plans to set up his own clinic in early June to serve patients.

Report from the YWCA Children's Health Clinic 161

The Children's Health Clinic conducted a total of 14 examinations over seven weeks from March 17 to April 24. 105 children were examined, with 53 receiving one examination, 18 receiving two examinations, and 34 children being vaccinated. 7% of the children had enlarged tonsils, 5% had trachoma, and 9% had coughs. According to the doctor, all the children with coughs did not have underlying conditions but were affected by the spring weather. The children who came to the clinic could be divided into three categories: 2% came for physical examinations, 6% came for treatment of illnesses, and 2% came for vaccinations. The clinic continues to offer examinations every Tuesday from 10:00 AM to 12:00 PM at the YWCA on Nanjing Road, and every Friday from 10:00 AM to 12:00 PM at the YWCA dormitory on Avenue Petain. All services are free.

Bicycle Race 164

Deng Yulin Falls and Dies

Deng Yulin, a chef from Xiang in a certain school on Hongqiao Road, rode his bicycle to the market early in the morning the day before yesterday to buy vegetables. While passing Haig Road, he raced another cyclist. As the bike was turning a corner, Deng suddenly fell to the ground. He barely opened his mouth to gasp, without saying a word, before his eyes closed and he passed away. The other cyclist left without looking back. Chen Xiaoer, a poor man who was collecting coal cinders by the roadside, saw Deng collapse and die. Unable to bear it, he went to report to the nearby constable. After inspecting the scene, the constable returned to the Jing'an Temple Police Station and reported to the head constable, who sent a detective to transport the body to the Fielun Road morgue. Yesterday morning, Qian, a prosecutor from the Special District Court, was commissioned to inspect the body. The deceased's wife, Mrs. Li, arrived and stated that her husband was thirty-five years old this year and had no previous illnesses. After her husband died yesterday, a man named Zhang told her that he was hit by a car. However, after Prosecutor Qian examined the body, he confirmed that Deng Yulin had indeed fallen and died before death. He ordered Mrs. Qian Li to claim the body for coffin and burial.

Accusation of Manufacturing Counterfeit Electrical Materials 165

Hu Guoguang, the owner of the China Battery Factory, represented by lawyers Jin Yu and Li Yuan, stated in the French court that the "53 Brand" dry battery produced by the plaintiff's factory is made of starch and has been registered with the former Ministry of Industry and Commerce for a five-year patent, which can be proven. Unexpectedly, the defendant, Ding Xiong Zhao He Cai and others in the battery factory set up inside counterfeited the plaintiff's brand. After the plaintiff's testing, the defendant also used starch in manufacturing, which is a deliberate imitation, causing a great impact on the plaintiff's business. The defendant violated the Trademark Law, requesting investigation and, in addition, granting incidental private prosecution to recover losses of 10,000 yuan. The defendants were also represented by lawyers who argued that the electrical materials produced in the defendant's factory are different from the plaintiff's trade name and trademark. The defendant's electrical materials are presented for inspection. As for the manufacturing method, the plaintiff uses starch, while the defendant uses gluten juice. The plaintiff's accusations have no evidence and should be dismissed. Judge Zhu ruled a deadline of fourteen days for the plaintiff to produce conclusive evidence for further verification.

Seduction of a Young Married Woman from a Neighboring Boat 166

Huang A'da, 48 years old, from Changzhou, residing at No. 614 Fuchang Lane near the Great World in the French Concession, has been working as a driver on a Westerner's small gasoline tanker. He has two married sons. His second daughter-in-law, Mrs. Su, is only in her early twenties and still quite beautiful. Because there was a lack of care on the boat, Huang, since this year, took his second daughter-in-law Su to the boat to take care of it, because his two sons were working outside. At the beginning of the third month of this year in the lunar calendar, when the boat was docked in the Suzhou River outside the Waitanyuan Bridge, Wu A'si and Tang Jinfang from another small gasoline boat met and became acquainted, because the boats were docked side by side and they passed each other from morning till night. On the eighth day, Huang took his wife to the hospital to see a doctor. When he returned to the boat, he suddenly found the boat empty. His second daughter-in-law, Mrs. Su, was missing. The small gasoline boat parked next to it had also sailed away. Huang then inquired from the neighboring boats and learned that Tang Jinfang had sailed away first, and Wu A'si had enticed Ms. Su to go with him. Huang then searched everywhere, but found no trace. It wasn't until 11:00 AM yesterday that Huang spotted Wu and Tang hiding in the boat along the Suzhou River in front of the Zhaofeng Garden in the West Shanghai. He got off the boat and dragged them to the shore, calling the police back to the Sixth District Police Station. After the District Chief's separate preliminary hearing, Huang He Da testified, 48 years old, from Changzhou, the rest of the statement as above, and Wu A'si testified, 35 years old, from Kunshan, working on a gasoline boat, and Tang Jinfang testified, 21 years old, local, prevaricated and denied about conspiring to kidnap Mrs. Su, the District Chief learned the confession and judged that the case involved conspiring to kidnap a married young woman and decided to prepare the documents today and send them to the court for interrogation.

Dies After Ineffective Treatment

Hua Jinrong, a small worker from Tongzhou, 24 years old, at the Jinglun Silk Factory on Hengfeng Road, Zhabei, was working on the roof of the three-story building of the factory at 3:15 PM yesterday. The Amorous Affair of a Chauffeur 169

Affair with the Maid of His Employer's House

Reprimanded by His Employer and Committed Suicide by Poison

Li Guojun, a chauffeur from Yangzhou, 32 years old, at the Zhao family on Avenue Joffre in the French Concession, liked to be fond of women and recently had an affair with the Zhao family's maid, A Jin. On the evening of the seventh of this month, they consummated their affair in A Jin's bedroom. Unexpectedly, their secret was revealed and he was fired as a driver after being reprimanded by the employer. Li then returned home. Out of shame and indignation, he secretly took opium to commit suicide. His wife, Mrs. Lü, noticed it the next day and rushed him to Baolong Hospital for treatment, but the poison had penetrated deeply into his internal organs, and he died in the afternoon of this day. The Xinzha Police Station, after receiving a report from Baolong, sent detectives to transport the body to the Fielun Road morgue. Yesterday morning, Qian Hongye, a prosecutor from the Special District Court, was commissioned to inspect the body and inquired about the reason for the suicide from the deceased's wife, Li Lü. He ordered her to claim the body for coffin and burial.

The Murdered Man was a Lounger 170

Chopped Seven Times with an Axe and Shot Four Times

The Body Claimed by the Mistress After the Examination

At 10:45 PM the night before last, a young man was assassinated by enemies in the back door of No. 27 Baoyu Lane, French Concession. He was chopped down with axes and died on the spot. The murderers fled in a panic. Afterwards, the French Police sent detectives to transport the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Morgue for examination. The details of the examination have been recorded in yesterday's newspaper. It is now learned that the deceased was Lou Ashui from Hangzhou, 24 years old, who used to weave on a loom in Hangzhou. He came to Shanghai as a lounger not long ago. He had no residence in Shanghai. In the first month of this year in the lunar calendar, he met Wang Guibao, a woman from Nanjing (19 years old, currently pregnant), and cohabitated in a hotel. After the incident, the deceased's fellow villager notified his mistress, who went to the morgue yesterday morning to identify the body and reported it to the police. Subsequently, the Criminal Section of the French Police reported to Judge Zhu of the French Concession Court, who arrived at the morgue at 2:00 PM in the afternoon to inspect the body. The corpse's head and upper body were chopped seven times with an axe, and the lower abdomen and legs were shot four times. After the examination, he sat in a public position. First, the detective reported the previous situation and presented the seized murder weapon. After Mr. Zhu questioned the deceased's mistress, he ruled that the deceased, Lou Ashui, had been assassinated on the spot. Since no relatives of the corpse were found, the mistress, Wang Gui, was allowed to be responsible for the coffin and burial. The police were ordered to take photos of the body for the record and to arrest the murderer for investigation. Subsequently, fellow villagers raised funds to purchase clothing and a coffin for burial and temporarily placed the coffin in the guild hall, waiting for the mother of the corpse to claim it for burial.
