American Mail Ship President Cleveland Delayed Due to Fog 174

Ship Rescued By American Trading Company

The Pacific mail ship President Cleveland of the American Trading Company, which came to Shanghai from Little Luzon, arrived in Hong Kong first. As it was about to reach Hong Kong, it suddenly encountered heavy fog, and the ship ran aground. Yesterday, the local American Trading Company received a telegram from Hong Kong, stating that the ship had been towed out by a ship sent after the fog cleared, but the ship had suffered minor damage and needed to be repaired in the Hong Kong shipyard. The original plan was to come to Shanghai on the 15th and sail to San Francisco and New York, but it may not be possible by then. The cargo and passengers are safe and sound.

Cargo and Passengers Transferred

The ship is a special express mail ship directly to New York newly dispatched by American Trading, requiring only 36 days from Shanghai to reach. The speed is the fastest among the New York routes of the Pacific ships in Shanghai. There was a lot of export cargo this time, with tung oil alone accounting for 1,200 tons, and there were also quite a few items such as lake silk. Yesterday, the company had to temporarily withdraw the customs declarations of those who had already been declared and transfer them to other ships because it could not arrive in Shanghai as scheduled. Passengers who had already purchased tickets were also going through the procedures of transferring to other ships yesterday.

The Public Works Department Decided to Form a Municipal Committee 175

Nominated Committee Members

The issue of municipal openness in the Public Concession, after repeated discussions by the board of directors of the Public Works Department, has been decided to first form a committee to consider methods to expand the scope of municipal publicity. The candidates for the committee have also been nominated separately by the Public Works Department and the press, including Mr. Perle (representative of the Public Works Department), Mr. Kokes (representative of the news agency), Mr. Howard (representative of the English newspaper), Mr. Dong Xianguang (representative of the American newspaper), Mr. Wang Yingbin (representative of the Chinese newspaper), and Mr. Watanabe (representative of the Japanese newspaper). In addition, the Secretary-General of the Public Works Department will also attend the meeting for discussions. Its authority has been determined as studying and investigating various methods and reporting to the board of directors, so that municipal news can be provided to the public more thoroughly and quickly. It is expected that the chairman of the board, Mr. McKnaten, will formally convene the establishment meeting of the committee early next week. Currently, in order to gather ideas from all parties, taxpayers in the concession and representatives of periodical publications and other newspapers are requested to submit any suggestions to Mr. Frasser at the Public Works Department. The committee welcomes it very much.

Silk Factories are Not Yet Ready to Collect Cocoons 176

Due to the Influence of Adverse Weather

In Hangzhou, Shaoxing, and other places in Zhejiang, the silkworm season is earlier, but the weather this year is cold and rainy. Most of the early silkworms have failed. After the late silkworms hatched, the climate is still bad and the feeding is difficult. After the silkworms entered hibernation, it rained heavily for five or six days, and the weather was as cold as winter, causing the silkworms in the lush leaves to spit black foam and excrete yellow water due to eating wet leaves, and seven out of ten died of stiffness. No one in the silkworm trade is willing to rent, and those who exchange for cocoon coupons are only about 20%. In Lanxi, Yuhang, Linping, Chang'an, Haining, and other places, about 20 cocoon shops are expected to open for sale, but silk factories in Shanghai are rarely prepared to collect cocoons.

Bookbinding Workers Went on Strike Yesterday 177

Demanding a 40% Wage Increase

More than 1,200 workers from 85 Western-style and Chinese-style bookbinding workshops in this city, including Ma Hongji, went on strike voluntarily yesterday morning to demand changes in their treatment conditions. The Municipal Social Bureau has scheduled a mediation meeting today. The details are recorded as follows:

Reasons for the Strike

The bookbinding workers submitted 18 treatment conditions, which were approved by the general meeting on March 13. The most important of these was the first, that from April 1, 1931, regardless of contract or monthly work, all wages would be increased by 40% based on the current amount. After the Citizen Training Council approved it, they were asked to negotiate on their own first. After half a month, it was believed that the capitalists were not sincere in accepting. It was said that the final means would be used to deal with it. The day before yesterday, Geng Longxiang, the owner of Xin Yi Workshop in Lian Zhi Lane, Baoshan Road, had a dispute with worker Zhou Guangyan, which triggered a full-scale voluntary strike at 9:00 AM yesterday. The union's persuasion was ineffective.

Number of Participants

85 companies in the Chinese clothing industry including Ma Hongji, De Da, He Xing, Tang Pinji, Zhang Shunji, Xu Xiangji, Wang Yuji, Dai Chunji, Ma Baoji, Wang Shengji, Chen Xinji, Wang Hengji, Wang Jinji, Yan Puji, Sun Bingji, Feng Yiji, Lu Baoji, Ding Ji, Xu Ji, Qiu Peiji, and the western clothing industry including Rui Feng, Mao Haoji, Lou Chengji, Shi Yongji, Zhao Deji, Fu Youji, He Xing, Shen Guiji, etc. A total of more than 1,200 workers participated.

Authorities' Mediation

The Municipal Social Bureau believes that a strike by clothing workers once would affect local public security, in order to quickly resolve the matter, yesterday notified the Bookbinding Industry Association and the Bookbinding Industry Union to notify the Bureau that it would convene a mediation at 2:00 pm on May 13, and first notify this fact, nominating two responsible representatives to the Bureau to await mediation.

Anti-Drug Meeting Resolves Seven Important Cases 178

The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association held its May Standing Committee meeting yesterday. Wang Yingqi, Li Denghui, Cai Runuo, Ding Shujing, Guo Baoyi, Huang Jiaohui, and others attended. Wang Jingqi chaired the meeting as usual. First, the Secretariat reported on the progress of work in April and the transportation of the association's anti-drug exhibits to anti-drug groups in Java for public display. (1) Following the report that Ms. Huang Baizhiying, the director general of the association, was previously falsely accused of drug trafficking by villains, in addition to the standing committee of the association issuing a statement to prove the truth, the Party Headquarters and the Hong Kong government subsequently proved that the rumors were unfounded. The truth has been published in Chinese and foreign newspapers based on the facts, and anti-drug groups from all over the world have also sent letters of condolence and defended her. The truth has already been revealed. However, the villains who spread the rumors and slander, their purpose was originally to destroy the anti-drug movement. Not only did this plan fail, but they may have changed their tactics and launched attacks by despicable means. How should we respond to this case? It was discussed to observe changes in the environment and find ways to respond at any time. (2) It was resolved that the association previously established a special committee to preside over the association's affairs when Director General Huang left Shanghai and rumors of Mrs. Bai's drug trafficking arose. Now that the truth about Bai's false accusation has been revealed and Director General Huang has long since returned to the association, the special committee's mission has also ended. From today onwards, the committee should be cancelled. (3) The Secretariat reported that the preparation office of the Tianjin Anti-Drug Association was not operating in accordance with the regulations, and the association entrusted Mr. Cao Hongzhu to go to sort it out to maintain the association's reputation and emphasize anti-drug efforts. According to a telegram from Cao, after arriving in Tianjin, he first visited all parties and took over the preparation office, reorganizing it into the Hebei Anti-Drug Association. All parties supported the preparatory committee, which has now been recognized by the Hebei Provincial Party Headquarters and received Permit No. 101. The association's reputation has now been restored and progress is going very smoothly. A letter of commendation should be sent to Representative Cao. However, although the organization and purpose of the local organizations are the same as those of the association, the content organization often varies due to circumstances, which often causes misunderstandings from the outside world due to the system. How should we respond to this? It was discussed that most of the local anti-drug organizations are promoted by enthusiastic people in the local area and are not established by the association's personnel. According to the regulations, they should be referred to as a certain local landlord.

Anti-Drug Association or Anti-Drug Propaganda Association does not need to be called Anti-Drug Branch to clarify the truth. (4) Director General Huang Jiaohui reported that Lu Zhengxiang, the former Premier of the State Council, recently sent a letter from the Pope of Rome commending the association's work, expressing great sympathy for our country's national anti-drug movement. It was resolved to send a letter to the Pope of Rome to thank him for his praise. (5) It was resolved to send representatives to contact the leaders of the local Catholic Church and ask them to send the Pope's opinion on the anti-drug movement to national church leaders, and to invite the Catholic Church to participate in anti-drug efforts and work together to promote the early success of the opium ban. (6) It was resolved to submit an opinion to the International League of Nations Conference on the Restriction of Narcotics and mail it to Europe immediately, and to consider the situation and urge colleagues staying in Europe to represent the association at the meeting in the vicinity. (7) The members of the national college thesis competition judges handed over to the secretariat for appointment. There is also a letter from the Singapore Anti-Drug Association, stating that the association's work is progressing actively and there is an urgent need for talent, requesting the association to send a secretary to assist the association for several months, which will be decided at the next meeting.

Central Bank Inspection Report 179

89th Time

The 89th inspection report on the issuance reserve of the Central Bank states: This council, in accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Ordinance, is responsible for inspecting the reserve for the issuance of convertible notes of the bank. The 89th inspection was held on May 9th, 1931, at the Issuance Bureau of the bank. The results of the inspection are hereby announced as follows: (A) Total amount of convertible notes issued: 32,685,100 silver dollars, including 31,280,312 silver dollar notes and 1,400,788 subsidiary currency notes. Total amount of convertible note reserve: 32,685,100 silver dollars, including cash reserve of 25,452,501.1 silver dollars. This cash reserve includes 18,089,543.35 silver dollars stored in the bank's issuing vault, 2,314,056 silver dollars stored in branch banks in various ports, and 5,048,901.75 silver dollars stored with other banks. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 7,232,598.9 silver dollars. (B) Customs Gold Unit convertible notes: total amount issued: 815,737.20 Customs Gold Units. Total amount of Customs Gold Unit convertible note reserve: 815,737.20 Customs Gold Units, including 13,595.62 taels of standard gold, with a fixed price of 0.60, equivalent to the above amount of Customs Gold Units. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Convertible Note Regulations, the cash reserve should be 60% and the guarantee reserve 40%. The inspection results show that the cash reserve exceeds 60% and the guarantee reserve is less than 40%, which is in accordance with the regulations. This report is hereby made. May 9th, 1931. Li Fusun, Chairman of the Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank; Supervisors: Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jiying.

Medical and Pharmaceutical Colleges Approved for Restoration 182

Chen Fangzhi, Xia Shenchu, Wu Guanmin, Liu Buqing, Zhu Qiluo, etc., standing committee members of the Medical and Pharmaceutical Society of the Republic of China, submitted a case to the National Government, the Central Party Headquarters, the Executive Yuan, the Legislative Yuan, and the Ministry of Education, requesting the revision of the medical and pharmaceutical education system and the restoration of medical and pharmaceutical specialized colleges. Now, a reply has been received from the Ministry of Education as follows: Received the report. It is noted that the Ministry promulgated regulations for specialized colleges in August of the 18th year of the Republic (1929), which included provisions for pharmaceutical specialized colleges. The recent revision of these regulations has added an item for medical specialized colleges. The report has been submitted to the Executive Yuan and forwarded to the National Government for record, and is being notified to all departments and bureaus, all specialized colleges, and all on record. Therefore, the Ministry of Education, in addition to the university regulations that stipulate medical colleges or independent college medical departments, also permits the establishment of medical and pharmaceutical specialized colleges. The old medical and pharmaceutical specialized schools can be reorganized and continued based on their original foundation, in accordance with the Organization Law of Specialized Colleges and the Revised Regulations for Specialized Colleges. You are hereby notified. This reply.

Jiangxi Charitable Organizations Send Telegrams Begging for Relief 184

Red Cross Receives Report

Raising Funds to Rescue Abandoned Infants

The Chinese Red Cross Society recently received a joint telegram from the Jiangxi Moral Branch and the Jiangxi Disaster Relief Association, stating: "In Jiangxi Province, crops have failed for years in a row. Due to floods, droughts, and wars, and in recent years, the rampant activities of the Red Bandits, looting, burning, and killing, blood has filled the valleys, and floating corpses are still visible in the rivers. One cannot take a step without encountering nets. Travelers still lament, like birds clinging to their branches, who will stop them? Cries of sorrow echo across the fields. Nine out of ten houses are empty, and the sounds of chickens and dogs are not heard along the way. Suffering a hundred sorrows and a thousand calamities, there are no plowing oxen to return to the fields. The disaster is truly the worst in the world, and fundraising is always running dry. The hope for life has been exhausted, and the future is even more difficult. We, the colleagues, are deeply saddened by what we see, and our hands are exhausted from helping. Fulfilling the duties of our homeland and upholding the conscience of morality, we dare to appeal to the billions of disaster victims, to the ten thousand homes of living Buddhas, hoping that gentlemen and people of benevolence, both at home and abroad, will show great compassion and provide extensive relief. A drop of willow branch sprinkled is like sweet rain. Streams from the mountains will converge into a great swamp. The urgency of the telegram is beyond words as we await your orders." Signed by Zhang Luchun, Xu Henian, Zeng Zhanggui, Wang Yunrong, Ding Lizhong, Zhang Shu, Zhang Xianqing, Hu Siyi, Wang Wenxuan, Xu Yuting, Lu Fang, Hong Benli, Xu Zhaolin, Wu Zhaochen, Ou Zufou, Cai Jin, Zhou Renlin, Gong Shicai, Xiong Yuhua, Zhao Congyi, Zhu Wu, Zou Rikui, bowing in gratitude. Printed for circulation.

The Chinese Red Cross Society considers the relief of infants as one of the active tasks of the International Red Cross Society. In China, apart from the existing orphanages in various places, there are no specially established institutions. According to a report from a certain charitable organization in Jiangxi, wherever the Communist Party goes, they burn and loot the wealth and treasures of the rich, and then the heads of the families are often shot, leaving behind more than 130 infants. They are temporarily being cared for by a certain charitable organization, but due to insufficient funds and a lack of wet nurses, the Chinese Red Cross Society has donated 1,000 yuan to purchase supplies needed for childcare, and plans to establish a model orphanage near Ganzhou, Jiangxi, to raise these infants.

Recent Report on Shaanxi Relief by the Jisheng Society 185

The Chinese Jisheng Society previously received a report from its Shaanxi relief commissioner, Mr. Li Yunmen, stating that the methods for surveying the disaster areas have been recorded in previous reports. Now, the number of households and detailed circumstances have been identified in each town, and a detailed report is being submitted in sections as follows: (1) Wugong Zhenyuan Town: 2,854 households surveyed. Weigong Town: 1,713 households. Youfeng Town: 1,301 households. Yangling Town: 2,322 households. Yongan Town: 1,057 households. Urban Area: 1,023 households. The above six towns have been surveyed, totaling approximately 10,270 disaster-stricken households. Relief funds and grain have already been distributed, and a separate letter has been submitted. (2) It is planned to survey the entire town of Changning. The three towns of Dazhuang, Xuegu, and Pujiji will be surveyed specifically in the highlands, as these three towns are adjacent to Changning and Zhenyuan Towns. Currently, Changning, Dazhuang, Xuegu, and Pujiji have begun the survey, which is expected to be completed within three weeks, and a detailed report will be submitted again. However, the number of disaster-stricken households in the surveyed towns has increased compared to the past, for three reasons: (1) Consecutive years of disaster have led to a gap between the old and new harvests, turning the poor into the extremely poor. (2) People who were displaced in the past are now returning home after hearing about the survey and relief. (3) People who previously fled to the north and south mountains have returned home to receive seeds and grain. They can now settle down and farm after receiving two rounds of timely rain. It is reported that three batches totaling 60,000 yuan were previously remitted to Wugong Zhenyang. After deducting 2,000 yuan for Jingyang Zhenyang, 3,400 yuan for the Wugong Disaster Children's Shelter, and 4,000 yuan for Qian County burial expenses, a total of 8,400 yuan was deducted. Therefore, the funds for seeds and emergency relief in various towns in Wugong are insufficient and will require additional allocations. When needed, an immediate request will be telegraphed for appropriation to meet the urgent needs. Upon arrival, the society's relief funds were completely depleted. Practical planning is now underway to provide immediate relief. It is said that after the seeds were distributed in Wugong, there have been two rounds of timely rain, so fortunately the planting was not delayed, saving the disaster-stricken households from starving again.

Bao Fang Exquisite Chinese and Western Furniture 186

Bao Fang Company, located at the eastern end of East Xinjiao Bridge on Avenue Edward VII, in addition to distributing gramophones and records, also employs artistic experts to create exquisite Chinese and Western decorative furniture and provide custom design services. All the decorative furniture inside the new building of the Shanghai Bank was planned by the company. The magnificent beauty embodies artistry. In addition, those who have entrusted the company to handle matters for various cinemas and Peking opera houses have all praised its work.

Zhenye Trading Company Appoints a Talented Manager 187

Zhenye Trading Company, a French-owned business located at 29 Sichuan Road, Shanghai, specializes in airships, military equipment, Western instruments, Western medicine, cosmetics, electrical refrigerators, electrical materials, fertilizer, and Western bricks. It has now hired Mr. Ma Zaimin as the General Manager for Chinese affairs. Mr. Ma is a prominent figure in the legal profession and has held important government positions. He has extensive experience in commerce. With such a talented person at the helm, the future development of the company's business is assured.

Labor Union for Newspaper Delivery Workers Handles Funeral for Member Sun 188

The Shanghai Newspaper Delivery Workers' Union reported that member Sun Zhongxi died of illness in Shanghai on the 10th of this month at 8:00 p.m. The union's relief department handled the funeral arrangements and purchased a coffin, spending 35 yuan, which was paid from the relief fund. On the 11th, the coffin was sent to the Sanguantang Cemetery in Caohejing for temporary burial, preparing to have Sun's family members come to Shanghai to claim the coffin for burial. Sun Zhongxi's ancestral home is in Zhuangxing Town, Fengxian County, Jiangsu Province, but the specific address is unknown. An inquiry has been sent, and the family members are requested to come to Shanghai as soon as possible to claim the coffin for burial.

Dr. Peter to Lecture at the Union Pacific Association 189

Since Dr. Peter was hired by the Chinese government to assist the Ministry of Health in formulating health education programs, the Union Pacific Association of this city is now scheduled to hold a luncheon meeting at the Old Carlton on the 18th at 12:15 p.m., inviting Dr. Peter to lecture on "The Management of the Plague in China." Those who wish to hear the famous speech should reserve seats with the association secretary as soon as possible.

News from Various Labor Unions 190

The Seamen's General Union held a regular meeting yesterday, chaired by Zhao Zhizhi. (A) Matters reported: (omitted) (B) Matters discussed: (1) A letter from Wu Branch Secretary Mo Zuoming reported that Wu Asheng and others of the Jiangshun Wheel were accused of pushing Huang Changgui to his death. The situation of the trial was requested for investigation. It was ordered that the middle cabin office be informed. (2) The Shanghai Branch reported that the wage method for various vessels under the China Merchants Bureau should be implemented by Shen Huating, the compradore of the Jiangtian Wheel. Approved. (3) The Guangdong Branch reported that He Chao and others of the Longshan Wheel were wrongly dismissed by customs officers. After the Guangdong Civil Affairs Department transferred the letter for reinstatement, it still needs further negotiations to be realized. The case was requested for investigation. Stored. (4) A letter from Huang Yongquan, the former Xiamen Branch Secretary, reported on his service to the seamen and the current difficulties of the union. He requested a way to be assigned work. He was ordered to wait for review and assignment. (Rest omitted)

The First District Shipbuilding Industry Labor Union held its seventh council meeting yesterday, chaired by Shu Hongshi. Matters discussed: (1) A difficult issue arose regarding members' dues due to the wage increase. Should it be changed? Resolution: (A) Still collect 1% according to the union constitution. (2) Add a clause during the contract revision period to request the factory to deduct it from the wages. (2) A person in charge should be designated to handle the formal signing of the new contract. Resolution: Officially appointed directors are responsible. (3) Request the Social Affairs Bureau to convene labor and management to sign conditions on a regular basis. Resolution: Passed. (4) Workers in the lifting department of the Quxin Factory were laid off in large numbers by the factory. If the work is slack, it should be handled in accordance with the autonomous regulations. Resolution: Passed. (5) The Quxin Factory's excessive use of apprentices hinders the livelihood of workers. Measures should be taken to stop it. Resolution: Negotiate with the factory. (6) Director Wang Chenghong resigned. Resolution: Retained. (7) Approve the appointment of Comrade Zhang Xinchang as secretary. Resolution: Passed.

The Toothbrush Industry Labor Union held its sixth joint meeting of supervisors and directors, chaired by Liu Zupei. Matters discussed: (1) The issue of appropriately increasing wages for female workers in the bone-shaving department and polishing department of the Yixin Factory. Resolution: Liu Zupei, Yang Rulin, and one representative from each department will be appointed to negotiate with the factory. (2) The Yixin Factory's lack of work subsidies for February and March. Request that the factory issue them as before. Resolution: Same as before. (3) How to sign the labor-management contract for the Zhenyu Factory. Resolution: Appoint Su Shaotao, Liu Ruixiang, Qian Jinglu, and Ou Changan to go. (4) Schedule a special membership meeting. Resolution: The time will be set this month. The location will be notified after it is decided. (5) Whether the joint meeting schedule will remain the same. Resolution: It will remain the same. (6) Member Wang Dabao requested medical treatment from the factory due to illness. Resolution: The clerk from the first branch office will negotiate.

Weather Report 191

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 p.m. yesterday stated: "The Yangtze River Basin and coastal areas will be sunny with heavy fog. Between the Ryukyu and Ogasawara Islands, the weather is bad with cyclones. The Shandong coast has southwest winds." Also, the temperature in this city in the 24 hours before 3:00 p.m. yesterday was 71.9°F maximum and 49.1°F minimum. On the same day last year, the maximum was 68.0°F and the minimum was 60.9°F.

Shanghai Market

Market News 192

The Anquan Firm proclaims that the Yang Brand record oil manufactured by the firm has been popular throughout the country since its launch. All those who have used this oil have praised it highly. Proof letters have been arriving daily in recent days, demonstrating the effectiveness of this oil in protecting records, which is indeed incomparable to other adhesives on the market. As a result, inquiries and purchases have been pouring in from various ports such as the Nanyang Islands, Pingjin, Sichuan, Hubei, Hunan, and Guangdong, to meet market demand. In addition to having the special effect of protecting records and gramophones, this oil can also be used to lubricate clocks, instruments, cameras, and all commercial typewriters, daily hardware, wooden furniture, etc. Once used, it ensures smooth and easy operation and long-lasting durability, truly making it the only essential product on the market for protecting records, gramophones, and all machinery. The price is only 60 cents per bottle. All major gramophone companies in this city are agents for its sale. The main distributor is located at Weianfang, Haining Road, this city.

The Wantai Limited Company proclaims that it is now selling a "Jierwen" boiler powder, which is the most suitable product for preventing iron scale from forming inside boilers and removing existing iron scale. The water used in boilers often contains minerals, which over time harden into iron scale and adhere to the inner surface of the boiler shell, reducing the boiler's heat transfer ability, wasting fuel, and damaging the boiler surface. The life of the boiler is thus shortened, and sometimes there is a risk of explosion due to slightly higher pressure. Using this powder can avoid all these problems, and the price is extremely low, requiring very little each time. It can be used in any type of water and is absolutely not like other iron scale prevention products, which have more harm than good. Even softened water needs to be added with a little of this powder to completely remove the remaining minerals. Therefore, it is truly a great contribution to the industrial world.

The Chinese Staff Association of the American Shenchang Foreign Firm proclaims that since its organization, the association has spared no effort in its management and operations, and its affairs are thriving. Recently, it has also launched a monthly publication called "Lianyizhi Guang," which is co-edited by Mr. Yu Xinyan and Mr. Lu Shixiong. The content includes editorials, academic knowledge, special articles, etc. Its purpose is to promote justice and to allow outsiders to understand the organization of the association. It is truly an innovative undertaking for Chinese staff in foreign firms to manage publications.

The Babicock & Wilcox Boiler Company proclaims that its London headquarters signed a contract with a power plant last month to undertake the construction of eight water-tube boilers, along with automatic coal feeders, etc. Each boiler can generate 256,000 pounds of steam per hour, with a steam pressure of 650 pounds per square inch, worth a total of 700,000 British pounds.

The British China Soap Company's main factory on Yangshupu Road in East Shanghai proclaims that the factory was built in 1924 and expanded in 1929, occupying a huge area of 150 acres. The main gate faces the Huangpu River, and the approximately 15,000 to 20,000 tons of raw materials required annually can be easily imported through this gate, taking full advantage of the geographical convenience. The factory is managed by British merchants, and the chairman and manager, Mr. E. H. Jones, is a talented person with rich experience in the business world. The factory is well-managed and neatly arranged, and it adheres to the principle of small profits and quick turnover, so its business is growing daily. Now, on the occasion of adding a fragrance soap factory, which is specially prepared for manufacturing Lux fragrance soap, merchants and journalists from various ports both domestic and foreign are specially invited to visit. The general manager, Mr. Jones, and the factory manager, Mr. Hobert, led the tour. The factory is large in scale and utilizes the latest machinery everywhere to replace manual labor. Therefore, it can produce 1.5 million boxes of soap annually, and only a little over 300 workers are needed. The factory has a total of 26 soap kettles, including 20 large kettles, each of which can boil 50 tons of soap, and the remaining small kettles can boil 25 tons. The steam room has 10 steam furnaces, burning approximately 50 to 60 tons of coal daily. The steam required for most soap kettles is supplied by this furnace. Other equipment such as printing presses, wooden box nailing machines, and printing presses that can print five sets of colors at the same time are all available. The comprehensiveness of the equipment is second to none among all factories in Shanghai. The soaps currently produced include Lever Sunlight Soap, Sanitary Medicinal Soap, Lux Toilet Soap, Lever Soap Powder, Xiangmao Beiji, and Hexing Umbrella Brand Soap, especially Sunlight, Xiangmao, and Beiji, which are the most popular. Furthermore, the main ingredients purchased by the factory, such as vegetable oils, are mostly sourced from China. The office staff, engineers, chemists, and workers employed are also all Chinese.
